bitcoin_magazine_1770694641000_9171638|1770694641000|2026|2|7|2026-02-09|bitcoin_magazine|Fed’s Waller Shrugs Off Bitcoin Volatility, Says Crypto Crashes Don’t Threaten Banks|<p><a href="https://bitcoinmagazine.com" rel="nofollow">Bitcoin Magazine</a><br />
<img src="https://bitcoinmagazine.com/wp-content/uploads/2026/02/Feds-Waller-Shrugs-Off-Bitcoin-Volatility-Says-Crypto-Crashes-Dont-Threaten-Banks.jpg" style="display: block; margin: 1em auto;" /><br />
<a href="https://bitcoinmagazine.com/news/feds-waller-shrugs-off-bitcoin-volatility" rel="nofollow">Fed’s Waller Shrugs Off Bitcoin Volatility, Says Crypto Crashes Don’t Threaten Banks</a></p>
<div id="bsf_rt_marker"></div>
<p>Federal Reserve Governor Christopher J. Waller downplayed risks from bitcoin and broader crypto markets on Monday, arguing that digital assets remain largely disconnected from the traditional financial system even as the technology behind them moves into the mainstream.</p>



<p>Speaking at an <a href="https://www.youtube.com/live/byRsdmhuheg" rel="noopener" target="_blank">event</a> hosted by the Global Interdependence Center, Waller framed crypto markets as an extension and competition of everyday commerce rather than an entirely new phenomenon.&nbsp;</p>



<p>His comments come as crypto markets continue to grapple with <a href="https://bitcoinmagazine.com/news/senate-banking-committee-clarity-act">regulatory uncertainty</a> in Washington and recurring bouts of <a href="https://bitcoinmagazine.com/news/bitcoin-price-plunges-toward-60000">volatility</a> that have shaped investor sentiment for years. While bitcoin has become more embedded in institutional portfolios, Waller suggested that price swings remain part of the market’s character rather than a systemic concern.</p>



<p>“Ups and downs in the crypto world have become so common they actually have a name for them: winters,” he said. “It’s part of the game.”</p>



<p>Waller dismissed recent declines in bitcoin’s price as less dramatic when viewed through a longer lens, noting that levels once considered extraordinary are now treated as routine.</p>



<p>“People like, oh my god, bitcoin’s down to 63,000,” he said. “Eight years ago, if you just said it was 10,000 you would have said, oh my god, this is crazy.”</p>



<figure class="wp-block-embed is-type-rich is-provider-twitter wp-block-embed-twitter"><div class="wp-block-embed__wrapper">
<blockquote class="twitter-tweet"><p dir="ltr" lang="en">JUST IN: <img alt="🇺🇸" class="wp-smiley" src="https://s.w.org/images/core/emoji/16.0.1/72x72/1f1fa-1f1f8.png" style="height: 1em;" /> Federal Reserve Governor Christopher Waller says Bitcoin volatility is just &quot;a part of the game.&quot;<br /><br />&quot;It's happened before. Bitcoin is down to $63,000. Eight years ago if you would have said it was $10,000, you would have said this is crazy!&quot; <a href="https://t.co/fTgZrHlaYY">pic.twitter.com/fTgZrHlaYY</a></p>&mdash; Bitcoin Magazine (@BitcoinMagazine) <a href="https://twitter.com/BitcoinMagazine/status/2020942247089389858?ref_src=twsrc%5Etfw" rel="noopener" target="_blank">February 9, 2026</a></blockquote>
</div></figure>



<p>The Fed governor also pushed back against the idea that <a href="https://bitcoinmagazine.com/markets/federal-reserve-enters-a-new-crypto-era">crypto volatility poses immediate threats to banks</a> or the broader payments system. In his view, crypto remains a separate ecosystem that can experience sharp crashes without triggering spillovers into traditional finance.</p>



<p>“These things are pretty detached from the traditional finance world,” he said. “You can have these big crashes and move volume. The rest of us wake up and we’re fine the next day. Nothing bad&#8217;s going on. The banks are open. Your payments are being made.”</p>



<p>Waller said he does not closely monitor crypto markets as part of his day-to-day responsibilities at the central bank, describing the sector as still outside the core of the financial system.</p>



<p>“The banks are open. Your payments are being made,” he said.</p>



<p>Early on in his talk, Waller compared a typical blockchain transaction to buying an apple at the grocery store, with different objects and different rails but the same basic structure of payment, execution, and recordkeeping.</p>



<p>“In the decentralized crypto world, a crypto asset, or digital asset, is the object that people want to buy,” Waller said, pointing to bitcoin and other tokens. The transaction, he argued, relies on new technologies such as blockchains, tokenization, and smart contracts, which he described as tools rather than threats.</p>



<p>“Those are just technologies,” Waller said. “There’s nothing dangerous about them. There’s nothing to be afraid of.”</p>



<h2 class="wp-block-heading">Waller: Bitcoin and crypto are becoming more commonplace</h2>



<p>At the same time, Waller acknowledged that crypto markets have begun to intersect more with mainstream finance, particularly as traditional firms explore blockchain-based infrastructure. He pointed to efforts by financial institutions and even the U.S. Treasury to <a href="https://www.sec.gov/newsroom/speeches-statements/uyeda-remarks-asset-management-derivatives-forum-020926" rel="noopener" target="_blank">consider</a> tokenized securities trading that could operate around the clock.</p>



<p>The ability to support 24/7 global trading, he said, represents one of the key innovations of blockchain-based systems compared with legacy banking infrastructure built around business hours and slower clearing cycles.</p>



<p>“These technologies were built to do this globally, 24 by seven from the beginning,” Waller said. “They’re not legacy systems.”</p>



<p>He argued that this constant trading and settlement capability is already forcing traditional financial institutions to improve their own payment systems, especially in cross-border transfers where crypto rails can move value without relying on established networks.</p>



<p>“They’re forcing the big banks, everybody else, to sort of make their payments, especially cross border, faster and cheaper,” he said.</p>



<p>Waller also highlighted the need for clearer regulatory definitions around digital assets, including whether various tokens should be treated as securities or commodities. He said that responsibility lies with Congress, the Securities and Exchange Commission, and the Commodity Futures Trading Commission.</p>



<p>“The bigger problem is clarity,” Waller said, adding that progress in Congress appears stalled. “Everybody thought clarity would come in that would clear the road,” he said. “It doesn’t look like it’s going anywhere anytime soon.”</p>



<p>Waller suggested that some of the recent cooling in crypto market enthusiasm reflects fading expectations that sweeping legislation would arrive quickly.</p>



<p>“The lack of passing of the clarity act has kind of put people off,” he said.</p>



<p>While Waller emphasized that bitcoin and speculative crypto assets are not his focus as a central banker, he offered blunt advice to investors navigating the sector’s volatility.</p>



<p>“Prices go up. Prices go down,” he said. “If you don’t like it, don’t get in.”</p>
<p>This post <a href="https://bitcoinmagazine.com/news/feds-waller-shrugs-off-bitcoin-volatility" rel="nofollow">Fed’s Waller Shrugs Off Bitcoin Volatility, Says Crypto Crashes Don’t Threaten Banks</a> first appeared on <a href="https://bitcoinmagazine.com" rel="nofollow">Bitcoin Magazine</a> and is written by <a href="https://bitcoinmagazine.com/authors/micahzimmerman" rel="nofollow">Micah Zimmerman</a>.</p>|https://bitcoinmagazine.com/news/feds-waller-shrugs-off-bitcoin-volatility|etf,regulation,macro,institutional,defi,selloff|BTC,ETH,MATIC|negative|1.0|1770720414922
bitcoin_magazine_1770686426000_9443799|1770686426000|2026|2|7|2026-02-09|bitcoin_magazine|Bitcoin Rebounds from $60K Capitulation Low, Eyes $74,500 Resistance This Week|<p><a href="https://bitcoinmagazine.com" rel="nofollow">Bitcoin Magazine</a><br />
<img src="https://bitcoinmagazine.com/wp-content/uploads/2026/02/bullish-price-thumbnail.webp" style="display: block; margin: 1em auto;" /><br />
<a href="https://bitcoinmagazine.com/markets/bitcoin-rebounds-from-60k-capitulation-low-eyes-74500-resistance-this-week" rel="nofollow">Bitcoin Rebounds from $60K Capitulation Low, Eyes $74,500 Resistance This Week</a></p>
<div id="bsf_rt_marker"></div>
<p><strong>Bitcoin Price Weekly Outlook</strong></p>



<p>Well, that escalated quickly! The bitcoin price just melted all the way through the $70,000s and $60,000s last week, but finally found its footing at $60,000. The bulls battled back from down there to push the price back up to $71,700 before it moved back slightly to close the week out at $70,315. The bears covered a lot of ground to the downside last week, so the bulls will try to get back some ground this week. Expect $60,000 support to hold at least into this week.</p>



<figure class="wp-block-image size-large"><img alt="Bitcoin Rebounds from $60K Capitulation Low, Eyes $74,500 Resistance This Week" class="wp-image-50376" height="730" src="https://bitcoinmagazine.com/wp-content/uploads/2026/02/image-3-1024x730.png" title="Bitcoin Rebounds from $60K Capitulation Low, Eyes $74,500 Resistance This Week 1" width="1024" /></figure>



<p><strong></strong><strong>Key Support and Resistance Levels Now</strong></p>



<p>With such a big move down last Thursday, we will need to find new resistance levels to watch going forward. Over the short term, $71,800 is a level to watch after the price rejected there Friday into Saturday. Above here, we have the 0.382 Fibonacci retracement from the latest move down, sitting at $74,500. If the price can manage to climb above this level, $79,000 should be a strong resistance. $84,000 sits firmly above this level and should be very strong resistance going forward.</p>



<p>Looking below, the bulls will look to hold $65,650 in order to try to put in the reversal here. $63,000 sits just below here as support. Next, we have $60,000 as newfound support just above the 0.618 Fibonacci retracement at $57,800. Arguably, the true support sits at $57,800 here and was slightly front-run at that $60,000 low. If this level is lost, we will look all the way down to $44,000 for support, then $39,000 at the 0.786 Fibonacci retracement below here.</p>



<p><strong>Outlook For This Week</strong></p>



<p>The MRI Indicator gave us a buy signal on Friday last week on the daily chart off of the $60,000 low. The move was strong from that level, so the bulls will have to try to capitalize on this bounce to continue the momentum into this week. This signal can produce a full reversal, but often only results in a 1 to 4 candle correction of the trend. So if the bulls can keep the push higher going into Wednesday, we may be looking at a sustainable reversal on the daily chart, which could attempt to reclaim the $80,000 level.</p>



<figure class="wp-block-image size-large"><img alt="Bitcoin Rebounds from $60K Capitulation Low, Eyes $74,500 Resistance This Week" class="wp-image-50377" height="730" src="https://bitcoinmagazine.com/wp-content/uploads/2026/02/image-4-1024x730.png" title="Bitcoin Rebounds from $60K Capitulation Low, Eyes $74,500 Resistance This Week 2" width="1024" /></figure>



<p><strong></strong><strong>Market mood: </strong>Bearish – The price lost a lot of ground last week. The bears are in control. Period.</p>



<p><strong>The next few weeks<br /> </strong>The bears took the price down another big leg last week. Weekly RSI hit oversold levels and produced a big bounce. After such a significant drop and such a big bounce back from $60,000, the price should remain constrained within a range here for at least the next few weeks. Do not expect to see any price action above $80,000 or below $60,000 for the next few weeks.</p>



<figure class="wp-block-image size-large"><img alt="" class="wp-image-50378" height="730" src="https://bitcoinmagazine.com/wp-content/uploads/2026/02/image-5-1024x730.png" title="Bitcoin Rebounds from $60K Capitulation Low, Eyes $74,500 Resistance This Week 3" width="1024" /></figure>



<p><strong></strong><strong>Terminology Guide:</strong></p>



<p><strong>Bulls/Bullish: </strong>Buyers or investors expecting the price to go higher.</p>



<p><strong>Bears/Bearish: </strong>Sellers or investors expecting the price to go lower.</p>



<p><strong>Support or support level: </strong>A level at which the price should hold for the asset, at least initially. The more touches on support, the weaker it gets and the more likely it is to fail to hold the price.</p>



<p><strong>Resistance or resistance level: </strong>Opposite of support.&nbsp; The level that is likely to reject the price, at least initially. The more touches at resistance, the weaker it gets and the more likely it is to fail to hold back the price.</p>



<p><strong>Oscillators:</strong> Technical indicators that vary over time, but typically remain within a band between set levels. Thus, they oscillate between a low level (typically representing oversold conditions) and a high level (typically representing overbought conditions). E.G., Relative Strength Index (RSI) and Moving Average Convergence-Divergence (MACD).</p>



<p><strong>RSI Oscillator:</strong> The Relative Strength Index is a momentum oscillator that moves between 0 and 100. It measures the speed of the price and changes in the speed of the price movements. When RSI is over 70, it is considered to be overbought. When RSI is below 30, it is considered to be oversold.</p>



<p><strong>Fibonacci Retracements and Extensions: </strong>Ratios based on what is known as the golden ratio, a universal ratio pertaining to growth and decay cycles in nature. The golden ratio is based on the constants Phi (1.618) and phi (0.618).</p>



<p><strong>Momentum Reversal Indicator (MRI):</strong> A proprietary indicator created by Tone Vays. The MRI indicator tracks buyer and seller momentum and exhaustion, providing signals to indicate when to expect momentum to fade and accelerate.</p>

bitcoin_magazine_1770683996000_1873476|1770683996000|2026|2|7|2026-02-09|bitcoin_magazine|Cipher Mining (CIFR) and TeraWulf (WULF) Get Morgan Stanley Nod; Marathon (MARA) Rated Underweight|<p><a href="https://bitcoinmagazine.com" rel="nofollow">Bitcoin Magazine</a><br />
<img src="https://bitcoinmagazine.com/wp-content/uploads/2026/02/Cipher-Mining-CIFR-and-TeraWulf-WULF-Get-Morgan-Stanley-Nod-Marathon-MARA-Rated-Underweight.jpg" style="display: block; margin: 1em auto;" /><br />
<a href="https://bitcoinmagazine.com/news/cifr-and-wulf-get-morgan-stanley-nod" rel="nofollow">Cipher Mining (CIFR) and TeraWulf (WULF) Get Morgan Stanley Nod; Marathon (MARA) Rated Underweight</a></p>
<div id="bsf_rt_marker"></div>
<p>Morgan Stanley initiated coverage of three publicly traded bitcoin miners on Monday, <a href="https://x.com/matthew_sigel/status/2020836948177248703">assigning</a> Overweight ratings to Cipher Mining (CIFR) and <a href="https://bitcoinmagazine.com/tags/terawulf">TeraWulf</a> (WULF) while giving Marathon Digital (MARA) an Underweight rating.</p>



<p>The move reflects the bank’s view that certain miners are better valued as infrastructure plays rather than pure crypto or bitcoin bets.</p>



<p>Analyst Stephen Byrd and his team set price targets of $38 for Cipher and $37 for TeraWulf. Shares of CIFR rose roughly 134% to $16.50 on Monday, while WULF climbed 13% to $16.20.&nbsp;</p>



<p>Marathon shares increased slightly to $8.28, below its $8 target.</p>



<p>Morgan Stanley’s thesis focuses on the transformation of bitcoin mining sites into data center assets.&nbsp;</p>



<p>Byrd <a href="https://www.coindesk.com/markets/2026/02/09/cipher-mining-and-terawulf-are-buys-mara-a-sell-as-morgan-stanley-begins-bitcoin-miner-coverag" rel="noopener" target="_blank">argued</a> that once a miner has built a data center and signed a long-term lease with a creditworthy counterparty, the asset should be valued for stable, long-term cash flow rather than bitcoin exposure.&nbsp;</p>



<p>He likened these sites to data center real estate investment trusts (REITs) such as Equinix (EQIX) and Digital Realty (DLR), which trade at high multiples due to scale and predictable revenue.</p>



<p>Cipher Mining sits at the <a href="https://bitcoinmagazine.com/markets/iren-cipher-cifr-mining-stock-soar">center of that framework</a>. Byrd described its facilities as suited to what he called a “REIT endgame,” where leased data centers function like toll roads, generating predictable cash flows with minimal reliance on bitcoin’s price.&nbsp;</p>



<p>TeraWulf also fits the model, with a track record of signing data center agreements and management experience in power infrastructure. The firm plans to expand 250 megawatts of data center capacity per year through 2032, with Morgan Stanley modeling success rates of 50% in a base case and 75% in an optimistic scenario.</p>



<p>Marathon Digital received a more cautious assessment. Byrd noted the company’s hybrid approach, combining bitcoin mining with data center ambitions, limits upside potential from bitcoin-to-data center conversions.&nbsp;</p>



<p>Marathon’s focus on acquiring bitcoin and issuing convertible notes to fund mining positions makes its value largely dependent on bitcoin prices.&nbsp;</p>



<p>Morgan Stanley highlighted the company’s limited history of hosting data centers and the historically low return on invested capital in bitcoin mining as factors in the Underweight rating.</p>



<h2 class="wp-block-heading">Bitcoin mining or AI?</h2>



<p>The coverage comes amid ongoing debate over whether bitcoin miners should evolve into power and AI. Morgan Stanley’s stance is selective: miners with long-term leased data centers may offer higher, more predictable returns, while those focused on mining remain exposed to cryptocurrency volatility.</p>



<p>Bitcoin miners are reallocating money and operational focus away from proof‑of‑work hashpower toward artificial intelligence and high‑performance computing data centers, as shrinking mining margins and halving‑driven revenue pressures make traditional operations less lucrative.&nbsp;</p>



<p>Major publicly traded miners such as <a href="https://bitcoinmagazine.com/news/bitfarms-to-exit-bitcoin-mining">Bitfarms</a> (now rebranded as Keel Infrastructure) and IREN <a href="https://bitcoinmagazine.com/bitcoin-mining/iren-stock-soars-bitcoin-mining-firm-surges-on-wall-street-ai-cloud-optimism">have signaled</a> full or partial exits from legacy mining to host AI workloads and secure long‑term contracts with cloud and hyperscaler partners.</p>
<p>This post <a href="https://bitcoinmagazine.com/news/cifr-and-wulf-get-morgan-stanley-nod" rel="nofollow">Cipher Mining (CIFR) and TeraWulf (WULF) Get Morgan Stanley Nod; Marathon (MARA) Rated Underweight</a> first appeared on <a href="https://bitcoinmagazine.com" rel="nofollow">Bitcoin Magazine</a> and is written by <a href="https://bitcoinmagazine.com/authors/micahzimmerman" rel="nofollow">Micah Zimmerman</a>.</p>|https://bitcoinmagazine.com/news/cifr-and-wulf-get-morgan-stanley-nod|regulation,layer2,mining,pump|BTC,ETH,SUI,OP|neutral|1.0|1770720414925
bitcoin_magazine_1770677318000_2358206|1770677318000|2026|2|7|2026-02-09|bitcoin_magazine|Bernstein Calls Current Bitcoin Selloff the ‘Weakest Bear Case in History,’ Reaffirms $150K Target for 2026|<p><a href="https://bitcoinmagazine.com" rel="nofollow">Bitcoin Magazine</a><br />
<img src="https://bitcoinmagazine.com/wp-content/uploads/2026/02/Bernstein-Calls-Current-Bitcoin-Selloff-the-‘Weakest-Bear-Case-in-History-Reaffirms-150K-Target-for-2026.jpg" style="display: block; margin: 1em auto;" /><br />
<a href="https://bitcoinmagazine.com/markets/bernstein-calls-bitcoin-selloff-weak" rel="nofollow">Bernstein Calls Current Bitcoin Selloff the ‘Weakest Bear Case in History,’ Reaffirms $150K Target for 2026</a></p>
<div id="bsf_rt_marker"></div>
<p>Bernstein analysts reiterated a bullish long-term outlook for bitcoin, calling the current <a href="https://bitcoinmagazine.com/markets/bitcoin-falls-over-59000-in-large-dip">bitcoin price downturn</a> the “weakest bear case” in the asset’s history and maintaining a $150,000 price target by the end of 2026.</p>



<p>The research and brokerage firm <a href="https://www.theblock.co/post/389003/weakest-bitcoin-bear-case-in-history-bernstein-reiterates-150000-price-target" rel="noopener" target="_blank">argued</a> that the recent drawdown reflects a crisis of confidence rather than structural damage to bitcoin’s network or investment thesis.</p>



<p>“What we are experiencing is the weakest bitcoin bear case in its history,” the analysts wrote, adding that none of the typical catalysts behind past crypto winters have emerged.</p>



<p>Bernstein said previous bear markets were driven by major failures, hidden leverage, or systemic breakdowns. This cycle, the firm sees no comparable blowups or widespread insolvencies.</p>



<p>Instead, analysts pointed to growing institutional alignment as a key difference. They cited support from a pro-bitcoin U.S. political environment, expanding adoption of spot BTC ETFs, rising corporate treasury participation, and continued involvement from large asset managers.</p>



<p>The firm argued that <a href="https://bitcoinmagazine.com/news/strategy-mstr-adds-1142-bitcoin">bitcoin’s broader adoption story</a> remains intact despite market weakness.</p>



<p>Bernstein also addressed criticism that bitcoin has lagged gold during the latest period of macro volatility. They said BTC continues to trade primarily as a liquidity-sensitive risk asset rather than a mature safe haven.</p>



<p>They noted that elevated interest rates and tighter financial conditions have concentrated gains in select areas such as precious metals and AI-linked equities.&nbsp;</p>



<p>Bernstein said BTC ETF infrastructure and corporate capital-raising channels remain positioned to absorb renewed liquidity if conditions ease.</p>



<p>Reporting from <a href="https://www.theblock.co/post/389056/polymarket-sues-massachusetts-state-federal-fight-prediction-markets" rel="noopener" target="_blank"><em>The Block</em></a> helped with the coverage of this analysis.</p>



<h2 class="wp-block-heading">Bernstein stays bullish on bitcoin; quantum fears dismissed.</h2>



<p>The analysts also pushed back against claims that BTC is losing relevance in an economy <a href="https://bitcoinmagazine.com/news/bitcoin-miner-cango-sells-millions-in-btc">shaped by artificial intelligence.</a></p>



<p>They argued that blockchains and programmable wallets could play a central role in an emerging “agentic” digital environment, where autonomous software agents require global, machine-readable financial rails. Traditional banking systems, they said, remain constrained by closed APIs and legacy integration barriers.</p>



<p>On quantum computing, Bernstein acknowledged that future cryptographic threats warrant preparation but said BTC is not uniquely exposed. </p>



<p>The firm argued that all critical digital systems face similar risks and will transition toward quantum-resistant standards together.</p>



<p>These thoughts echo that of <a href="https://bitcoinmagazine.com/tags/strategy">Strategy</a>, on Strategy’s fourth-quarter 2025 earnings call, Executive Chairman Michael Saylor <a href="https://bitcoinmagazine.com/news/strategy-mstr-will-lead-bitcoin-effort">said</a> the company will launch a Bitcoin Security Program aimed at coordinating with the broader cyber and crypto community.&nbsp;</p>



<p>The message echoed Strategy’s view that quantum computing is not an immediate threat, but a future engineering challenge that the network will have time to address.</p>



<p>Saylor framed <a href="https://bitcoinmagazine.com/news/jefferies-bitcoin-over-quantum-computing">quantum fears</a> as the latest version of “FUD,” arguing that many major industries still rely on the same cryptographic foundations BTC uses today. He pointed to ongoing global investment in quantum-resistant research and said the Bitcoin ecosystem is already exploring upgrades that could strengthen the protocol if needed.</p>



<p>He emphasized that any major change would require broad global consensus, consistent with Bitcoin’s history of adapting through technical and regulatory pressure.</p>



<p>Bernstein added that BTC&#8217;s transparent codebase and the growing involvement of well-capitalized stakeholders position it to adapt alongside other financial and governmental systems.</p>



<p>Bernstein also dismissed <a href="https://bitcoinmagazine.com/markets/strategy-stock-plummets-8-percent">concerns about leveraged corporate bitcoin accumulation</a> and the risk of miner capitulation.</p>



<p>The analysts said major bitcoin-holding firms have structured liabilities to withstand prolonged downturns.&nbsp;</p>



<p>They pointed to comments from Strategy executives that only an extreme scenario — BTC falling to $8,000 and remaining there for five years — would require balance sheet restructuring.</p>



<p>Bernstein maintained that the selloff represents sentiment weakness rather than systemic failure, and reiterated its forecast for bitcoin to reach $150,000 by the end of 2026.</p>



<p>At the time of writing, BTC is trading slightly below $70,000.</p>

bitcoin_magazine_1770674124000_9800149|1770674124000|2026|2|7|2026-02-09|bitcoin_magazine|Bitcoin Miner Cango Sells Millions in Bitcoin to Cut Debt and Fund AI Expansion|<p><a href="https://bitcoinmagazine.com" rel="nofollow">Bitcoin Magazine</a><br />
<img src="https://bitcoinmagazine.com/wp-content/uploads/2026/02/Bitcoin-Miner-Cango-Sells-Millions-in-Bitcoin-to-Cut-Debt-and-Fund-AI-Expansion.jpg" style="display: block; margin: 1em auto;" /><br />
<a href="https://bitcoinmagazine.com/news/bitcoin-miner-cango-sells-millions-in-btc" rel="nofollow">Bitcoin Miner Cango Sells Millions in Bitcoin to Cut Debt and Fund AI Expansion</a></p>
<div id="bsf_rt_marker"></div>
<p>Cango (CANG) <a href="https://www.prnewswire.com/news-releases/cango-inc-completes-bitcoin-sale-to-strengthen-financial-position-and-advance-ai-transformation-302682507.html" rel="noopener" target="_blank">said</a> it sold 4,451 Bitcoin over the weekend for net proceeds of about $305 million as the company moves to strengthen its balance sheet and support a shift into artificial intelligence infrastructure.</p>



<p>The Dallas-based Bitcoin miner announced Monday that the transaction was settled directly in Tether’s USDT stablecoin.&nbsp;</p>



<p>The company said the full amount of the proceeds was used to partially repay a Bitcoin-collateralized loan.</p>



<p>Cango said the sale followed a review of market conditions and was approved by its board of directors. The <a href="https://bitcoinmagazine.com/featured/corporate-bt-treasuries-are-underwater">company</a> framed the move as a balance-sheet adjustment aimed at reducing leverage rather than a retreat from its mining business.</p>



<p>The company&#8217;s stock is currently down 9%. </p>



<p>“The divestment of a portion of the Company’s Bitcoin holdings was executed to strengthen its balance sheet and reduce financial leverage,” Cango said in its statement.</p>



<p>The company said the debt reduction provides greater capacity to fund its strategic expansion into AI compute infrastructure. Cango is pursuing a plan to build an integrated energy and AI compute platform by using its grid-connected mining sites to provide distributed computing services for the AI industry.</p>



<p>The bitcoin miner said its approach will roll out in phases. The first stage will deploy modular, containerized GPU compute nodes across existing sites. The company said it plans to offer inference capacity for small and medium enterprises, a segment it described as underserved.</p>



<p>A later phase will focus on building a software orchestration platform to unify distributed compute resources across its global footprint.</p>



<h2 class="wp-block-heading">Cango’s AI and bitcoin miner pivot</h2>



<p>As part of the AI push, the bitcoin miner announced the appointment of Jack Jin as chief technology officer of its AI business line. </p>



<p>The company said Jin previously worked at Zoom Communications, where he led deployments of multi-node GPU clusters supporting large language model inference and fine-tuning. Cango said his background aligns with its roadmap to build a distributed inference platform.</p>



<p>Cango said its AI development leverages existing strengths in computing operations and energy management. The company added that it remains committed to its Bitcoin miner operations, with continued focus on improving mining economics and balancing hashrate scale with operational efficiency.</p>



<p>The sale comes as <a href="https://bitcoinmagazine.com/news/bitfarms-to-exit-bitcoin-mining">mining firms face tighter margins</a> following the Bitcoin halving cycle, rising power costs, and price volatility.&nbsp;</p>



<p>Public miners have <a href="https://bitcoinmagazine.com/bitcoin-mining/iren-stock-soars-bitcoin-mining-firm-surges-on-wall-street-ai-cloud-optimism">begun exploring</a> AI and high-performance computing as alternative revenue streams tied less directly to Bitcoin market cycles.</p>



<p>Cango entered the digital asset space in November 2024 and operates bitcoin miner sites across North America, the Middle East, South America, and East Africa. </p>



<p>The company also continues to run an online international used car export business through AutoCango.com. Cango said it will maintain a disciplined framework for asset allocation as it pursues long-term value creation while advancing its AI transformation.</p>

bitcoin_magazine_1770665755000_6101637|1770665755000|2026|2|7|2026-02-09|bitcoin_magazine|Strategy (MSTR) Adds 1,142 Bitcoin for $90 Million as Bitcoin Trades Near $69,000|<p><a href="https://bitcoinmagazine.com" rel="nofollow">Bitcoin Magazine</a><br />
<img src="https://bitcoinmagazine.com/wp-content/uploads/2025/12/Strategy-MSTR-Buys-Nearly-1-Billion-Worth-of-Bitcoin.jpg" style="display: block; margin: 1em auto;" /><br />
<a href="https://bitcoinmagazine.com/news/strategy-mstr-adds-1142-bitcoin" rel="nofollow">Strategy (MSTR) Adds 1,142 Bitcoin for $90 Million as Bitcoin Trades Near $69,000</a></p>
<div id="bsf_rt_marker"></div>
<p>Strategy bought another 1,142 bitcoin for about $90 million, extending its long-running accumulation campaign even as the company’s massive treasury remains underwater on paper.</p>



<p>The purchase was disclosed Monday in an 8-K <a href="https://x.com/strategy/status/2020846069374955535?s=46&amp;t=qcJDE0RaWiQjEKjMZF2JjA">filing</a> with the U.S. Securities and Exchange Commission. Strategy said it acquired the coins between Feb. 2 and Feb. 8 at an average price of $78,815 per bitcoin.</p>



<p>The latest buy lifts <a href="https://bitcoinmagazine.com/tags/strategy">Strategy’s</a> total holdings to 714,644 BTC. The stack is valued near $49 billion at current market prices. Strategy has spent roughly $54.4 billion to build the position, including fees and expenses.&nbsp;</p>



<p>The average purchase price across its holdings stands at $76,056 per bitcoin.</p>



<p>The company funded the acquisition through its ongoing at-the-market equity program. The company sold 616,715 shares of its Class A common stock, MSTR, for about $89.5 million last week. </p>



<p>As of Feb. 8, Strategy still had nearly $8 billion in share issuance capacity available under the program.</p>



<p>Michael Saylor, the company’s co-founder and executive chairman, signaled the purchase ahead of the filing with his usual Sunday post pointing to Strategy’s bitcoin tracker and the phrase “Orange Dots Matter.”</p>



<p>At the time of publication, Bitcoin is <a href="https://bitcoinmagazine.com/bitcoin-price">trading</a> near $69,000.</p>



<h2 class="wp-block-heading">Strategy ($MSTR) stock price volatility </h2>



<p>The buy comes after Strategy <a href="https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=1kyXKI0m_LI" rel="noopener" target="_blank">reported</a> a steep quarterly loss as the bitcoin pullback erased tens of billions of dollars in value from its balance sheet. The company <a href="https://bitcoinmagazine.com/markets/strategy-stock-plummets-8-percent">posted</a> one of the largest quarterly losses ever recorded by a U.S. public firm.</p>



<p>During the earnings call, CEO Phong Le addressed concerns around leverage and debt servicing. He said bitcoin would need to fall to $8,000 and remain there for five to six years before Strategy faced serious difficulty covering its convertible obligations.</p>



<p>Also during the call, Saylor <a href="https://bitcoinmagazine.com/news/strategy-mstr-will-lead-bitcoin-effort">said</a> the company will launch a Bitcoin Security Program to coordinate with the global cyber and crypto security community. He argued quantum computing is a long-term issue, not an immediate threat, and said any future Bitcoin upgrade would require broad global consensus.</p>



<p>Analysts remain divided on the approach. TD Cowen <a href="https://www.theblock.co/post/388821/strategy-is-better-positioned-than-ever-to-weather-bitcoin-crash-and-benefit-from-recovery-td-cowen-says" rel="noopener" target="_blank">said</a> Strategy has reinforced its position as the leading corporate bitcoin treasury company and could benefit from any market recovery. Bernstein analysts also argued the firm has structured liabilities conservatively, with no major debt maturities until 2028.</p>



<p>MSTR stock moved lower in premarket trading Monday, down more than 5%, as bitcoin struggled to hold above $69,000. The shares remain closely tied to bitcoin’s price swings, leaving investors watching both the company’s balance sheet and the broader crypto market.</p>

bitcoin_magazine_1770584400000_4546860|1770584400000|2026|2|6|2026-02-08|bitcoin_magazine|Bitcoin Price Reclaims $71,000 as Institutions Buy the Dip and Retail Interest Surges|<p><a href="https://bitcoinmagazine.com" rel="nofollow">Bitcoin Magazine</a><br />
<img src="https://bitcoinmagazine.com/wp-content/uploads/2026/02/Bitcoin-Price-Reclaims-71000-as-Institutions-Buy-the-Dip.jpg" style="display: block; margin: 1em auto;" /><br />
<a href="https://bitcoinmagazine.com/markets/bitcoin-price-71000-buy-the-dip" rel="nofollow">Bitcoin Price Reclaims $71,000 as Institutions Buy the Dip and Retail Interest Surges</a></p>
<div id="bsf_rt_marker"></div>
<p>The Bitcoin price climbed back <a href="https://bitcoinmagazine.com/bitcoin-price">above</a> $71,000 over the weekend, <a href="https://bitcoinmagazine.com/markets/bitcoin-price-roars-above-71000">extending</a> its rebound after one of the sharpest sell-offs of the cycle sent the price briefly plunging toward $60,000 earlier this week.</p>



<p>The recovery comes as institutional investors appear to be treating sub-$70,000 bitcoin as a renewed buying opportunity, even while retail traders search for signs the market has reached a bottom.</p>



<p>Bitwise CEO Hunter Horsley said in a CNBC interview that bitcoin’s pullback is landing differently with large investors than with long-time holders.</p>



<p>“I think long-time holders are feeling unsure,” Horsley <a href="https://www.cnbc.com/video/2026/02/05/crypto-is-getting-swept-up-with-rest-of-the-macro-bitwise-ceo-horsley.html" rel="noopener" target="_blank">said</a>. “And I think the new investor set, institutions are sort of getting a new crack at the apple.”</p>



<p>Horsley added that some institutional buyers are now seeing price levels they believed they had permanently missed, as bitcoin gets “swept up” in a broader macro-driven selloff across liquid risk assets.</p>



<h2 class="wp-block-heading">Retail traders are searching for a signal</h2>



<p>While institutions have been stepping in, retail participants have been scanning the market for confirmation that the sell-off has fully exhausted itself.</p>



<p>Sentiment platform Santiment <a href="https://app.santiment.net/insights/read/this-week-in-crypto-full-written-summary-w1-february-2026-10534?utm_source=weekly&amp;utm_medium=email&amp;utm_campaign=year2026week5" rel="noopener" target="_blank">said</a> in a weekend report that retail traders are “meta-analyzing” the downturn, looking for proof that others are quitting before re-entering the market — behavior that often emerges near market lows.</p>



<p>“Retail traders are trying to meta-analyze the market, looking for signs of others quitting to time their own entries,” Santiment wrote.</p>



<p>Google Trends data reflects the spike in attention. Worldwide searches for “Bitcoin” hit a score of 100 for the week starting Feb. 1 — the highest level in the past 12 months — as bitcoin’s price whipsawed from above $81,000 down to $60,000 before rebounding.</p>



<p>Searches for the term “crypto capitulation” also surged, rising from 11 to 58 in the week ending Feb. 8.</p>



<h2 class="wp-block-heading">Federal Reserve cuts are coming for the bitcoin price</h2>



<p>Adding to all this, ProCap Financial CIO Jeff Park <a href="https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=bZfsLFGz4hE" rel="noopener" target="_blank">suggested</a> bitcoin price’s next major bull-market catalyst may not come from Federal Reserve rate cuts — but from bitcoin’s ability to rise even in a tightening environment.</p>



<p>Park described a scenario where the bitcoin price climbs alongside higher interest rates as the asset’s “holy grail,” challenging traditional assumptions about liquidity and the global monetary system.</p>



<p>Last week, crypto exchange Bithumb <a href="https://bitcoinmagazine.com/news/bithumb-bitcoin-blunder-sends-44-billion">said</a> it accidentally sent out more than $40 billion worth of Bitcoin during a promotional rewards event after a payout error gave some users thousands of BTC instead of a small cash reward.</p>



<p>The exchange quickly restricted trading and withdrawals, recovering 99.7% of the excess Bitcoin and stressing the incident was not caused by hacking or a security breach. </p>



<p>A small amount — about 125 BTC worth roughly $9 million — remains unrecovered, and Bithumb said it will cover the losses with corporate funds.</p>



<p>Bitcoin price was trading above $71,400 at the time of publication, stabilizing after days of extreme volatility that rattled both crypto and broader financial markets.</p>



<figure class="wp-block-image size-large"><img alt="bitcoin price" class="wp-image-50362" height="1008" src="https://bitcoinmagazine.com/wp-content/uploads/2026/02/Bitcoin-Magazine-Pro-Screenshot-82-1024x1008.png" title="Bitcoin Price Reclaims $71,000 as Institutions Buy the Dip and Retail Interest Surges 4" width="1024" /></figure>
<p>This post <a href="https://bitcoinmagazine.com/markets/bitcoin-price-71000-buy-the-dip" rel="nofollow">Bitcoin Price Reclaims $71,000 as Institutions Buy the Dip and Retail Interest Surges</a> first appeared on <a href="https://bitcoinmagazine.com" rel="nofollow">Bitcoin Magazine</a> and is written by <a href="https://bitcoinmagazine.com/authors/micahzimmerman" rel="nofollow">Micah Zimmerman</a>.</p>|https://bitcoinmagazine.com/markets/bitcoin-price-71000-buy-the-dip|regulation,macro,institutional,hack,selloff,pump|BTC,NEAR|neutral|0.75|1770720414928
bitcoin_magazine_1770580584000_7105458|1770580584000|2026|2|6|2026-02-08|bitcoin_magazine|Bithumb Bitcoin Blunder Sends $44 Billion to Users, Rattles Crypto Markets|<p><a href="https://bitcoinmagazine.com" rel="nofollow">Bitcoin Magazine</a><br />
<img src="https://bitcoinmagazine.com/wp-content/uploads/2026/02/Bithumb-Bitcoin-Blunder-Sends-44-Billion-to-Users-Rattles-Crypto-Markets-.jpg" style="display: block; margin: 1em auto;" /><br />
<a href="https://bitcoinmagazine.com/news/bithumb-bitcoin-blunder-sends-44-billion" rel="nofollow">Bithumb Bitcoin Blunder Sends $44 Billion to Users, Rattles Crypto Markets </a></p>
<div id="bsf_rt_marker"></div>
<p>South Korean crypto exchange Bithumb <a href="https://bitcoinmagazine.com/news/bithumb-accidentally-sends-bitcoin-users">said it mistakenly distributed</a> more than $40 billion worth of Bitcoin to customers during a promotional rewards event, triggering sharp price volatility last week for bitcoin’s price.</p>



<p>The exchange said the incident occurred when a planned giveaway of small cash rewards was processed incorrectly. Instead of awarding about 2,000 Korean won, or roughly $1.40, some users received at least 2,000 Bitcoin each.</p>



<p>The error <a href="https://www.reuters.com/world/asia-pacific/crypto-firm-accidentally-sends-44-billion-bitcoins-users-2026-02-07/" rel="noopener" target="_blank">resulted</a> in the accidental distribution of roughly 620,000 Bitcoin, valued at approximately $44 billion at current prices.</p>



<p>Bithumb <a href="https://finance.yahoo.com/news/south-korean-crypto-exchange-accidentally-174618936.html" rel="noopener" target="_blank">apologized</a> for the mistake and said it has now recovered 99.7% of the excess Bitcoin. The exchange said it restricted trading and withdrawals for 695 affected customers within 35 minutes of the erroneous payout.</p>



<p>“We would like to make it clear that this incident is unrelated to external hacking or security breaches,” Bithumb said in a statement. “There are no problems with system security or customer asset management.”</p>



<p>Despite the quick response, reports said a small number of recipients sold or traded the coins before restrictions were imposed. Bithumb <a href="https://biz.chosun.com/stock/finance/2026/02/08/LNXJLG7B2BDCHIUC63JQYMBEB4/" rel="noopener" target="_blank">told</a> local media it had not yet recovered 125 Bitcoin, worth around $9 million, from a small group of customers.</p>



<p>The exchange said it would cover those remaining losses using its own corporate funds.</p>



<h2 class="wp-block-heading">Bithumb’s Bitcoin disruptions </h2>



<p>The incident caused an immediate disruption in Bitcoin trading on the platform. Charts from Bithumb showed Bitcoin briefly slumped 17% to 81.1 million won or roughly $55,000 during the selloff before recovering. The price later rebounded to around 104.5 million won.</p>



<p>South Korea’s financial regulators responded swiftly. The Financial Services Commission said the incident exposed vulnerabilities in the virtual asset sector. Officials said they would review internal control systems at domestic exchanges and launch on-site inspections if irregularities were found.</p>



<p>South Korean newspaper Kookmin Ilbo <a href="https://www.kmib.co.kr/article/view.asp?arcid=0029367457" rel="noopener" target="_blank">reported</a> regulators had already begun an inspection at Bithumb’s offices on February 7. Investigators reportedly requested a list of employees authorized to issue crypto payments.</p>



<p>Unnamed sources quoted by the newspaper described the incident as revealing “structural vulnerabilities” in the exchanges operational processes.</p>



<p>Reports indicated that Bithumb’s internal system allowed employees to issue loyalty points, Korean won, Bitcoin, and Ethereum without formal settlement procedures, increasing the risk of payout errors.</p>



<p>Executives acknowledged internal shortcomings. In an email to employees, Exchange Business Division Vice President Hwang Seung-wook <a href="https://www.dlnews.com/articles/markets/bithumb-to-write-off-125-million-in-bitcoin-losses-after-giveaway-gaffe/#:~:text=%E2%80%9CThe%20fact%20that%20a%20single,fail%20to%20prevent%20such%20errors.%E2%80%9D" rel="noopener" target="_blank">said</a> the mistake demonstrated weaknesses in the company’s processes.</p>



<p>“The fact that a single error in setting an event reward unit can destabilize an entire crypto exchange demonstrates the current state of our systems,” he wrote. He said the company would focus on eliminating failures in oversight rather than blaming individuals.</p>



<h2 class="wp-block-heading">Bithumb’s compensation plan</h2>



<p>Bithumb announced compensation measures for customers affected by abnormal trading conditions during the incident.</p>



<p>The exchange said users who sold Bitcoin at unusually low prices during the disruption would receive the full sale amount plus an additional 10%. Bithumb also said it would waive trading fees across all markets for seven days beginning February 9.</p>



<p>The company said it would provide 20,000 Korean won, or about $15, to customers who were actively using the platform at the time of the incident.</p>



<p>The error comes at a sensitive time for the exchange. The exchange has been pursuing plans to become the first South Korean crypto exchange to go public in the United States this year. </p>



<p>Earlier this month, South Korea’s consumer protection watchdog <a href="https://finance.yahoo.com/news/south-korea-consumer-watchdog-probes-171115911.html" rel="noopener" target="_blank">launched</a> a probe into Bithumb’s marketing claims.</p>



<p>For now, Bithumb is in damage control mode. The exchange has promised to compensate users who lost money from panic selling during the glitch. The company also says it will review and upgrade its internal systems to prevent future errors. Details on specific fixes have not yet been released.</p>
<p>This post <a href="https://bitcoinmagazine.com/news/bithumb-bitcoin-blunder-sends-44-billion" rel="nofollow">Bithumb Bitcoin Blunder Sends $44 Billion to Users, Rattles Crypto Markets </a> first appeared on <a href="https://bitcoinmagazine.com" rel="nofollow">Bitcoin Magazine</a> and is written by <a href="https://bitcoinmagazine.com/authors/micahzimmerman" rel="nofollow">Micah Zimmerman</a>.</p>|https://bitcoinmagazine.com/news/bithumb-bitcoin-blunder-sends-44-billion|regulation,hack,selloff|BTC,ETH,SOL,SUI|negative|0.95|1770720414929
bitcoin_magazine_1770423427000_443654|1770423427000|2026|2|6|2026-02-06|bitcoin_magazine|Strategy ($MSTR) Soars 25% as Bitcoin Rebounds|<p><a href="https://bitcoinmagazine.com" rel="nofollow">Bitcoin Magazine</a><br />
<img src="https://bitcoinmagazine.com/wp-content/uploads/2026/01/MSCI-Will-Not-Exclude-Bitcoin-Treasury-Companies-Like-Michael-Saylors-Strategy-From-Global-Indexes.jpg" style="display: block; margin: 1em auto;" /><br />
<a href="https://bitcoinmagazine.com/markets/strategy-soars-as-bitcoin-rebounds" rel="nofollow">Strategy ($MSTR) Soars 25% as Bitcoin Rebounds</a></p>
<div id="bsf_rt_marker"></div>
<p>Shares of Strategy ($MSTR) surged sharply Friday, lifting more than 25% at times, trading near $133, after a brutal prior session left the bitcoin‑linked stock <a href="https://bitcoinmagazine.com/markets/mstr-shares-sink-as-bitcoin-hits-72000">deeply oversold.</a>&nbsp;</p>



<p>The jump comes as markets stabilized and bitcoin rebounded from multi‑week lows to around $71,000, injecting newfound demand into equities tied to digital assets.</p>



<p>Friday’s rally reversed a dramatic sell‑off on Thursday, during which MSTR shares plunged to multi‑year lows on earnings losses and renewed pressure in crypto markets.&nbsp;</p>



<p>From a macro perspective, Strategy’s stock movement has tracked bitcoin’s sharp swings. As the leading corporate holder of bitcoin, MSTR’s <a href="https://bitcoinmagazine.com/news/strategy-falls-brace-for-earnings">performance</a> is highly correlated with BTC price action.&nbsp;</p>



<p>Declines in digital assets earlier in the week sent the stock tumbling, with bears pushing Strategy prices as low as the $105 range Thursday.&nbsp;</p>



<figure class="wp-block-image size-large is-resized"><img alt="strategy" class="wp-image-50355" height="874" src="https://bitcoinmagazine.com/wp-content/uploads/2026/02/Screenshot-2026-02-06-at-1.14.30-PM-1024x874.png" style="width: 336px; height: auto;" title="Strategy ($MSTR) Soars 25% as Bitcoin Rebounds 5" width="1024" /></figure>



<h2 class="wp-block-heading">Strategy’s earnings losses&nbsp;</h2>



<p>Strategy posted a $12.4 billion <a href="https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=1kyXKI0m_LI" rel="noopener" target="_blank">loss</a> for the fourth quarter of 2025, largely driven by unrealized declines in the value of its vast bitcoin holdings.</p>



<p>The headline loss dwarfed market expectations and weighed heavily on the share price, contributing to the Thursday slump.</p>



<p>Despite the earnings shortfall, executives remained committed to their long‑term bitcoin strategy.&nbsp;</p>



<p>Executive Chairman Michael Saylor said that the company is starting a Bitcoin Security Program to coordinate with global cyber and crypto communities, framing quantum computing as a long-term challenge unlikely to threaten Bitcoin for over a decade.&nbsp;</p>



<p>The company said that quantum fears are the latest form of Bitcoin “FUD,” noting ongoing global investment in quantum-resistant security and potential protocol upgrades through broad consensus.</p>



<p>Strategy’s leadership stressed resilience, saying the company could withstand extreme bitcoin price drops without immediate solvency concerns.&nbsp;</p>



<p>Executives, like CEO Phong Le, highlighted long-term strategy, ongoing capital raises, and confidence that Bitcoin will emerge stronger from future technological or market challenges.</p>



<p>Le said Bitcoin <a href="https://bitcoinmagazine.com/news/strategy-mstr-will-lead-bitcoin-effort">would need to fall</a> to around $8,000 per coin and stay at that level for five to six years before the company would face serious difficulty servicing its convertible debt.</p>



<p>“In the extreme downside, if we were to have a 90% decline in bitcoin price, and the price was $8,000, that is the point at which our bitcoin reserve equals our net debt,” Le said. He noted that under such conditions, the company could consider restructuring or raising additional capital.</p>



<figure class="wp-block-embed is-type-video is-provider-youtube wp-block-embed-youtube wp-embed-aspect-16-9 wp-has-aspect-ratio"><div class="wp-block-embed__wrapper">
<div class="youtube-embed"></div>
</div></figure>



<p>At the time of writing, the price of Bitcoin is $70,040, with a 24-hour trading volume of 157 B. BTC is 7% in the last 24 hours. </p>



<p>It is currently -2% from its 7-day all-time high of $71,258, and 16% from its 7-day all-time low of $60,256. BTC has a circulating supply of 19,985,218 BTC and a max supply of 21,000,000 BTC. <br /></p>

bitcoin_magazine_1770420362000_5670037|1770420362000|2026|2|6|2026-02-06|bitcoin_magazine|Bitcoin Price Roars Above $71,000 After Days of Sell-Offs|<p><a href="https://bitcoinmagazine.com" rel="nofollow">Bitcoin Magazine</a><br />
<img src="https://bitcoinmagazine.com/wp-content/uploads/2026/02/Bitcoin-Price-Roars-Above-70000-After-Days-of-Sell-Offs.jpg" style="display: block; margin: 1em auto;" /><br />
<a href="https://bitcoinmagazine.com/markets/bitcoin-price-roars-above-71000" rel="nofollow">Bitcoin Price Roars Above $71,000 After Days of Sell-Offs</a></p>
<div id="bsf_rt_marker"></div>
<p>The bitcoin price rebounded sharply Friday after a steep sell-off over the previous 24 hours, climbing briefly climbing above $71,000, a jump of $11,000 from its $60,000 low earlier in the 24-hour session. </p>



<p>The move came after several turbulent market sessions that saw the flagship cryptocurrency break key psychological support levels in a matter of hours. On Thursday, February 5, the Bitcoin price plunged as global financial markets deteriorated, with major stock indices sliding sharply and pushing investors out of riskier assets.&nbsp;</p>



<p>The sudden downturn was linked to broader macroeconomic stress, including weak earnings reports and steep declines in technology stocks, which intensified a flight to safety among traders.&nbsp;</p>



<p>Data compiled Thursday showed Bitcoin’s value dipping to its lowest since late 2024, signaling growing bearish sentiment among market participants.&nbsp;</p>



<p>The digital asset had retreated more than 40% from its all-time high above $126,000 reached in October 2025, underscoring the severity of the downturn.</p>



<p>Also, as the bitcoin price collapsed yesterday, forced liquidations boomed with <a href="https://bitcoinmagazine.com/news/bitcoin-price-plunges-toward-60000">over</a> $1 billion in positions wiped out over the past 24 hours, predominantly long bets facing automatic close-outs as BTC broke key levels.</p>



<h2 class="wp-block-heading">Crypto stocks rebound as Bitcoin price recovers</h2>



<p>Despite Thursday’s losses, Bitcoin price&#8217;s rebound Friday saw prices climb from the $60,000 region back above the $70,000 mark, reflecting a nearly 15% recovery from intraday lows.&nbsp;</p>



<p>Crypto-related stocks saw massive gains as well. Strategy ($MSTR) shares were up 21% on the day, while Coinbase ($COIN) and Circle ($CRCL) and Robinhood ($HOOD) shares all jumped 10-15%&nbsp;</p>



<p>Bitcoin-linked equities also posted sharp gains, led by MARA Holdings (MARA), which climbed 21.03% to $8.14, and TeraWulf (WULF), up 19.55% to $14.25. Riot Platforms (RIOT) rose 16.54% to $14.05, while Cipher Mining (CIFR) added 15.47% to $14.66.&nbsp;</p>



<p>Bitmine Immersion Technologies (BMNR) increased 15.43% to $20.08, and Core Scientific (CORZ) gained 10.43% to $16.36. Neptune Digital Assets (NDA) also advanced, rising 11.43% to $0.78</p>



<p>During the drop, the iShares Bitcoin Trust (IBIT), a spot Bitcoin ETF managed by BlackRock that lets investors gain exposure to Bitcoin without holding the crypto directly, crushed its daily volume record with about $10 billion worth of shares traded — even as its price <a href="https://x.com/EricBalchunas/status/2019522889435812298">plunged</a> 13%, marking the second‑worst one‑day drop since the fund’s launch.</p>



<p>Currently, bitcoin is trading at $70,661.&nbsp;</p>

cryptoslate_1770738024000_5877093|1770738024000|2026|2|7|2026-02-10|cryptoslate|The real drivers of XRP supply: A guide to understand Ripple’s monthly releases and what matters|<h2>XRP supply and escrow unlocks: a guide to modeling 2026 net flows</h2>
<p>XRP supply in 2026 hinges on how much escrowed XRP Ripple chooses to distribute after monthly unlocks.</p>
<p>The process is capped by the ledger, while market impact still depends on net flows and demand.</p>
<p>According to the XRP Ledger, total supply is fixed at <strong>100 billion XRP</strong>, while Ripple’s on-ledger escrow system sets an upper bound of <strong>1 billion XRP</strong> that can become available each month.</p>
<p>Unused amounts can be re-escrowed. For background, see XRPL’s <a href="https://xrpl.org/docs/introduction/what-is-xrp">“What is XRP?”</a>, the <a href="https://learn.xrpl.org/faq/what-is-the-total-supply-of-xrp/">total supply FAQ</a>, and the <a href="https://xrpl.org/blog/2017/explanation-of-ripples-xrp-escrow">XRPL escrow explainer</a>.</p>

    <a class="cs-article-embed__link" href="https://cryptoslate.com/xrp-etfs-top-1b-but-why-hasnt-price-moved/">
                    <div class="cs-article-embed__media">

            <h3 class="cs-article-embed__title">XRP’s $1 billion ETF record is misleading, and one hidden flow metric explains why price remains stagnant</h3>
                            <p class="cs-article-embed__summary">XRP ETFs have crossed $1B in AUM, yet XRP’s price has barely flinched. Here’s what that disconnect teaches you about how ETFs actually move markets.</p>
                                        <div class="cs-article-embed__meta">
                                            <span class="cs-article-embed__meta-item">Jan 3, 2026</span>
                                                                <span class="cs-article-embed__meta-divider">&middot;</span>

                                    </div>
                    </div>
    </a>
</div>

<hr />
<h3>Key takeaways</h3>
<ul>
<li>XRP’s maximum supply is capped at <strong>100 billion XRP</strong>, and 100 billion XRP existed at creation.</li>
<li>Ripple locked <strong>55 billion XRP</strong> into on-ledger escrows, designed to add supply predictability.</li>
<li>The escrow design releases up to <strong>1 billion XRP</strong> per month as an upper limit, and leftovers can be re-escrowed into later months.</li>
<li>XRPL transaction fees are burned, with a minimum fee of <strong>10 drops (0.00001 XRP)</strong> that can rise under load.</li>
<li>“Unlock” is not the same as “distribution,” and partial whale-tracker samples are not enough to compute a monthly net.</li>
</ul>
<h3>Who this is for</h3>
<ul>
<li>Long-term holders tracking dilution, escrow cadence, and market structure shifts (see: <a href="https://cryptoslate.com/one-billion-xrp-moved-from-ripples-escrow-mistaken-for-a-whale-dump/">escrow cadence coverage</a>).</li>
<li>Swing traders modeling month-to-month liquidity and exchange supply (see: <a href="https://cryptoslate.com/xrp-on-exchanges-hits-8-year-low-but-historical-data-exposes-a-brutal-flaw-in-the-popular-moon-narrative/">exchange balance framing</a>).</li>
<li>Institutional participants mapping hedging, custody concentration, and flow ceilings from escrow (see: <a href="https://cryptoslate.com/cme-group-announces-xrp-futures-fastest-contract-to-cross-1-billion-open-interest/">regulated derivatives context</a>).</li>
</ul>
<h3>What to watch this quarter</h3>
<ul>
<li>Full-month unlock and re-lock totals before estimating net new supply (avoid partial samples).</li>
<li>Fee regime changes during congestion since fees are burned and can escalate.</li>
<li>Escrow share versus circulating share from primary explorers or APIs at publish time (see <a href="https://docs.xrpscan.com/api-documentation/fact/facts-in-namespace">XRPSCAN facts endpoints</a>).</li>
<li>Changes in market structure that alter who holds XRP and how exposure is hedged (see Ripple’s <a href="https://ripple.com/insights/q1-2025-xrp-markets-report/">Q1 2025 XRP Markets Report</a>).</li>
</ul>
<hr />

    <a class="cs-article-embed__link" href="https://cryptoslate.com/one-billion-xrp-moved-from-ripples-escrow-mistaken-for-a-whale-dump/">

                <div class="cs-article-embed__body">
            <span class="cs-article-embed__related-reading">Related Reading</span>
            <h3 class="cs-article-embed__title">One billion XRP moved from Ripple's escrow mistaken for a whale dump</h3>
                                        <div class="cs-article-embed__meta">
                                            <span class="cs-article-embed__meta-item">Aug 2, 2019</span>
                                                                <span class="cs-article-embed__meta-divider">&middot;</span>
                                                                <span class="cs-article-embed__meta-item">Priyeshu Garg</span>
                                    </div>
                    </div>
    </a>
</div>

<h2>Supply overview</h2>
<p>XRP’s supply constraints start with a hard cap.</p>
<p>The XRP Ledger documentation describes XRP as capped at <strong>100 billion</strong>, and the ledger began with <strong>100 billion XRP</strong> created at inception.</p>
<p>The moving variable is not issuance; it is location and availability.</p>
<p>XRP can sit in escrow, in circulating balances, or in concentrated holdings that may trade infrequently.</p>
<p>“Circulating supply” is a headline number.</p>
<p>“Effective float” can be modeled as the portion that is practically available to trade at the margin (an editorial construct, not an XRPL-defined metric).</p>
<p><strong>Forward-looking frame:</strong> In a month where the escrow ceiling is <strong>1 billion XRP</strong>, the market outcome still depends on what fraction is distributed and where it lands, such as exchanges, market makers, or longer-term holders.</p>
<p>The escrow design itself notes that the amount of XRP actually released into circulation will likely be much less than the monthly maximum.</p>
<h2>Escrow schedule & releases</h2>
<p>Ripple locked <strong>55 billion XRP</strong> into a series of on-ledger escrows.</p>
<p>The structure was described as adding predictability to supply in Ripple’s 2017 <a href="https://ripple.com/insights/ripple-escrows-55-billion-xrp-for-supply-predictability/">escrow announcement</a>.</p>
<p>The ledger-side mechanics matter for forward estimates.</p>
<p>The escrow design releases a total of <strong>1 billion XRP</strong> per month across independent escrows.</p>
<p>It is explicitly described as an upper limit on how much XRP can become available from escrow in a given month.</p>
<p>Any unused XRP can be placed into a new escrow to be released later, preserving the ceiling while shifting timing.</p>
<p>Early February 2026 provided examples of these mechanics in public whale-tracking logs.</p>
<p>Whale Alert recorded <a href="https://whale-alert.io/transaction/ripple/B68819391C47C66EFEB94CBBFA8C73807410F0FF5920B5A111C7558FDBF6E14E">400 million XRP</a> and <a href="https://whale-alert.io/transaction/ripple/87D4E608B9A202C624C2CE6CC8087FEC232E3E36114948AAA1144625456B6155">100 million XRP</a> “unlocked at Ripple” on Feb. 1, 2026.</p>
<p>It then recorded <a href="https://whale-alert.io/transaction/ripple/D8|https://cryptoslate.com/the-real-drivers-of-xrp-supply-a-guide-to-understand-ripples-monthly-releases-and-what-matters/|etf,regulation,institutional,defi,whale,selloff|BTC,ETH,ADA,LINK,DOT,MKR,XRP,TRX|neutral|0.95|1770720435894
cryptoslate_1770687944000_3982397|1770687944000|2026|2|7|2026-02-09|cryptoslate|Ripple says compliance controls will unlock DeFi, but XRPL liquidity is still too thin to prove it|<p><a href="https://cryptoslate.com/companies/ripple/">Ripple</a> is working to make decentralized finance more familiar to regulated institutions and is placing <a href="https://cryptoslate.com/coins/xrp/">XRP</a> at the center of that effort.</p>
<p>DeFi’s earlier growth cycles were built around open, retail-facing liquidity pools and the associated risk tolerance. Total value locked across major protocols climbed into the tens of billions of dollars and, at previous peaks, surpassed $100 billion.</p>
<p>Ripple’s pitch is that the next phase will be shaped less by permissionless pools and more by controlled access, compliant settlement, and tokenized cash and collateral that institutions can recognize as market infrastructure.</p>
<p>In a February <a href="https://ripple.com/insights/institutional-defi-on-xrpl-scaling-real-world-finance-with-xrp-at-the-core/">blueprint</a>, Ripple described an institutional DeFi stack on the XRP Ledger (XRPL) that centers on stablecoin settlement, tokenized collateral, compliance controls, and an on-ledger credit layer, which is planned for later this year.</p>
<p>Rather than competing with the largest DeFi hubs on raw totals, Ripple is emphasizing primitives that align with how institutions already organize markets, including identity, access control, cash flows, and collateral settlement.</p>
<h2>Cash and collateral are scaling</h2>
<p>A key part of Ripple’s framing is that the most durable activity may sit outside traditional DeFi totals. Tokenized cash equivalents and high-grade collateral have expanded sufficiently to continue attracting attention even as speculative activity cools.</p>
<p><a href="https://app.rwa.xyz/">RWA.xyz</a>, which tracks tokenized real-world assets, reported a represented asset value of about $21.41 billion and a distributed asset value of nearly $23.87 billion. Its tokenized US Treasuries dashboard showed a total value of around $10.0 billion.</p>
<p><a href="https://cryptoslate.com/xrp-is-thriving-everywhere-except-on-its-own-chain/">Ripple is positioning XRPL</a> to align more closely with those flows. The blueprint highlighted features to support tokenized instruments and delivery-versus-payment workflows, while keeping access controls and compliance tooling close to the base layer.</p>
<p>Meanwhile, the extent to which large tokenization remains contested.</p>
<p>McKinsey has <a href="https://www.linkedin.com/posts/povilasrandis_mckinsey-report-tt-outlook-2025-activity-7359492125295599617-YJXk">estimated</a> that tokenized market capitalization across asset classes could reach about $2 trillion by 2030.</p>
<p>On the other hand, a separate BCG and ADDX <a href="https://addx.co/insights/bcg-addx-report-asset-tokenization-to-grow-50x-into-us-16-trillion-opportunity-by-2030/">report</a> forecast a larger opportunity, projecting that tokenization could reach about $16.1 trillion by 2030.</p>
<h2>What is live on XRPL, and what is still on the roadmap</h2>
<p>Ripple’s institutional argument hinges on a clear split between what the network can already support and what still has to ship.</p>
<p>The XRPL already runs meaningful transaction volume and has native exchange rails.</p>
<p>Messari <a href="https://messari.io/report/state-of-xrp-ledger-q4-2025">said</a> average daily transactions rose 3.1% quarter over quarter to about 1.83 million in the fourth quarter of 2025, while average daily active addresses slipped to about 49,000.</p>
<p>Payment transactions declined 8.1% to roughly 909,000, while offer creation grew to about 42% of the transaction mix.</p>
<p>Those figures do not, on their own, show institutional participation. But they matter to Ripple’s pitch because they indicate that the settlement and exchange layer is already used at scale, which reduces the burden on institutions to treat XRPL as an operating rail rather than a greenfield experiment.</p>
<p>Ripple said several components are already live, including Multi-Purpose Tokens, a token standard designed to carry metadata such as restrictions, and Credentials, which it describes as an identity layer for attaching attestations such as KYC status to participants.</p>
<p><a href="https://cryptoslate.com/xrpl-permissioned-domains-make-regulated-defi-more-real-and-the-first-battleground-will-likely-be-stablecoin-order-books/">Ripple also listed Permissioned Domains,</a> along with tooling such as Simulate and Deep Freeze, and an <a href="https://cryptoslate.com/xrp-ledger-launches-evm-sidechain-bridging-ethereum-and-xrp/">XRPL EVM sidechain</a>.</p>
<p>It also laid out a timetable for additional pieces, including a permissioned decentralized exchange in the second quarter, smart escrows and Multi-Purpose Token DEX integration in the second quarter, and confidential transfers for Multi-Purpose Tokens using zero-knowledge proofs in the first quarter.</p>
<p>The roadmap also includes a lending protocol based on the XLS-65 and XLS-66 specifications.</p>
<p>The near-term reporting test is whether measurable liquidity deepens before the later features arrive.</p>
<p>DefiLlama data showed <a href="https://cryptoslate.com/rlusd-supply-hit-1-26b-and-82-of-it-now-sits-on-ethereum-not-xrpl/">stablecoins circulating on XRPL</a> at roughly $418 million, with RLUSD accounting for about 83% of that total. It also showed the XRPL DEX at about $38.21 million in total value locked and about $15.08 million in 24-hour volume, with cumulative volume around $2.019 billion.</p>
<p>Those baselines are not large relative to the biggest DeFi venues, but they provide a concrete starting point for evaluating whether permissioned markets deepen, whether order books thicken, and whether routed volume rises once the roadmap items ship.</p>
<h2>Why XRP matters in the plumbing</h2>
<p>Ripple’s claim is that XRP’s relevance comes less from a burn narrative and more from how the ledger routes value.</p>
<p>On XRPL, transaction fees are paid in XRP and destroyed, a design meant to deter spam. The network’s base transaction cost is small, often described as 10 drops, and the protocol burns the exact fee specified when a transaction is included in a validated ledger.</p>
<p>For context, Messari quantified the fee channel's actual size. It said transaction fees, in dollars, fell to about $133,100 in the fourth quarter, and that native transaction fees declined to about 57,600 XRP.</p>
<p>It also said roughly 14.3 million XRP had been burned since the ledger’s inception, a low burn rate it tied to low per-transaction costs.</p>
<p>XRPL also uses reserves that can create structural demand for XRP as usage grows. Official XRPL documentation lists a base reserve of 1 XRP per account and an owner reserve of 0.2 XRP per item, which applies to objects such as trust lines and offers.</p>
<p>That said, Ripple’s argument implies that fee burn and reserves are not the primary levers. The larger story is liquidity routing.</p>
<p>XRPL’s decentralized exchange supports auto-bridging, which can use XRP as an intermediary when it reduces costs compared with trading two tokens directly.</p>
<p>This is where the institutional pitch becomes testable. If regulated stablecoin and FX pairs develop on a permissioned DEX, XRP could become inventory held by market makers to intermediate flows.</p>
<p>But the design does not guarantee that outcome. Auto-bridging is conditional, and direct stablecoin-to-stablecoin pairs can dominate if they offer better execution.</p>
<p>Ripple’s thesis rests on XRP becoming the preferred hop often enough that it functions as market-structure plumbing rather than a passive fee token.</p>
<h2>The stablecoin wedge and the credit question</h2>
<p>Ripple is leaning on stablecoins as the institutional on-ramp and forecasts diverge on how fast that market could grow.</p>
<p>JPMorgan analysts project that stablecoins could reach $500 billion by 2028, calling higher projections too optimistic. However, Standard Chartered has published a more aggressive outlook, e|https://cryptoslate.com/xrp-at-the-heart-of-ripples-institutional-defi-ambitions/|regulation,macro,institutional,defi,pump|ETH,ADA,LINK,NEAR,MKR,XRP|neutral|0.8|1770720435896
cryptoslate_1770678346000_6971095|1770678346000|2026|2|7|2026-02-09|cryptoslate|Why Bitcoin faces a brutal liquidity trap because China’s $298B of US Treasuries are up for sale|<p>China’s gradual retreat from US government debt is evolving from a quiet background trend into an explicit risk-management signal, and <a href="https://cryptoslate.com/coins/bitcoin/">Bitcoin</a> traders are watching the market for the next domino.</p>
<p>The immediate trigger for this renewed anxiety came on Feb. 9 when Bloomberg <a href="https://www.bloomberg.com/news/articles/2026-02-09/china-urges-banks-to-limit-holdings-of-us-treasuries-citing-market-volatility">reported</a> that Chinese regulators were urging commercial banks to limit their exposure to US treasuries, citing concentration risk and volatility.</p>
<p>This guideline immediately focuses attention on the massive pool of US bonds held by Chinese institutions. Data from the State Administration of Foreign Exchange show Chinese lenders’ holdings of dollar-denominated bonds at roughly $298 billion as of September.</p>
<p>However, a critical unknown and the source of market jitters is exactly how much of that figure is allocated specifically to Treasuries versus other dollar debt.</p>
<p>Meanwhile, this regulatory pressure on commercial lenders isn't happening in a vacuum. It compounds a year-long strategic retreat from US treasuries, already evident in Beijing's official accounts.</p>
<p>The US Treasury’s “Major Foreign Holders” <a href="https://tradingeconomics.com/united-states/foreign-treasury-holdings-china">data</a> show that mainland China’s official Treasury holdings fell to $682.6 billion in November 2025, the lowest level in the past decade.</p>
<figure class="wp-caption aligncenter" id="attachment_518954" style="width: 1000px;"><img alt="US Treasuries Held by China" class="size-full wp-image-518954" height="520" src="https://cryptoslate.com/wp-content/uploads/2026/02/Screenshot-2026-02-09-150219.jpg" width="1000" /><figcaption class="wp-caption-text" id="caption-attachment-518954">US Treasuries Held by China (Source: Trading Economy)</figcaption></figure>
<p>This continues a trend that has accelerated over the past five years, as <a href="https://cryptoslate.com/why-chinas-record-gold-bet-validates-bitcoin/">China has aggressively reduced its dependence on the US financial market.</a></p>
<p>Essentially, the combined picture is stark: the bid from the East is drying up across both commercial and state channels.</p>
<p>For Bitcoin, the threat isn’t that China will single-handedly “break” the Treasury market. The US market is simply too deep for that; with $28.86 trillion in marketable debt, China’s $682.6 billion represents just 2.4% of the stock.</p>
<p>However, the real danger is more subtle: if reduced foreign participation forces US yields higher via the term premium, it will tighten the very financial conditions that high-volatility assets like crypto depend on.</p>
<h2>The “term premium” channel is where things get interesting</h2>
<p>On the day the headlines broke, the US 10-year yield <a href="https://tradingeconomics.com/united-states/government-bond-yield">hovered around 4.23%</a>. While that level isn't inherently a crisis, the risk lies in how it could rise.</p>
<p>An orderly repricing is manageable, but a disorderly spike caused by a buyer strike can trigger rapid deleveraging across rates, equities, and crypto.</p>
<p>A 2025 economic <a href="https://www.kansascityfed.org/research/economic-bulletin/the-changing-investor-composition-of-us-treasuries-part-1-foreign-treasury-sales-could-raise-us-yields/">bulletin</a> from the Federal Reserve Bank of Kansas City offers a sobering assessment of this scenario. It estimates that a one-standard-deviation liquidation among foreign investors could spike Treasury yields by 25 to 100 basis points.</p>
<p>Crucially, it notes that yields can rise even without dramatic selling, as simply a reduced appetite for new issuance is enough to pressure rates higher.</p>
<p>Moreover, a more extreme tail-risk benchmark comes from a 2022 NBER working <a href="https://www.nber.org/system/files/working_papers/w30476/w30476.pdf">paper</a> on stress episodes. The study estimates that an &#8220;identified&#8221; $100 billion sale by foreign officials could shock the 10-year yield by more than 100 basis points on impact before fading.</p>
<p>This isn't a baseline forecast, but it serves as a reminder that during liquidity shocks, positioning dominates fundamentals.</p>
<h2>Why Bitcoin cares: real yields and financial conditions</h2>
<p>Bitcoin has traded like a macro duration asset for much of the post-2020 cycle.</p>
<p>In that regime, higher yields and tighter liquidity often translate into weaker bids for speculative assets, even when the catalyst begins in rates rather than crypto.</p>
<p>So, the real-yield component is vital here. With the US 10-year <a href="https://fred.stlouisfed.org/series/DFII10?">inflation-adjusted (TIPS) yield</a> at roughly 1.89% on Feb. 5, the opportunity cost of holding non-yielding assets is rising.</p>
<p>However, the trap for bears is that broader financial conditions are not yet screaming “crisis.” The Chicago Fed’s National Financial Conditions <a href="https://www.chicagofed.org/research/data/nfci/current-data">Index</a> sat at -0.56 for the week ending Jan. 30, indicating conditions remain looser than average.</p>
<p>This nuance is dangerous: markets can tighten meaningfully from easy levels without tipping into systemic stress.</p>
<p>Unfortunately for crypto bulls, that intermediate tightening is often enough to knock Bitcoin lower without triggering a Fed rescue.</p>
<p>Notably, <a href="https://cryptoslate.com/bitcoin-short-term-holders-are-panic-selling-at-a-loss-but-was-this-capitulation-or-just-a-leverage-reset/">Bitcoin’s recent price action</a> confirms this sensitivity. Last week, the flagship digital asset <a href="https://cryptoslate.com/bitcoin-whales-are-dumping-massive-amounts-of-supply-on-exchanges-as-liquidations-mirror-the-2022-ftx-market-collapse/">briefly fell below $60,000</a> amid broad risk-off moves, only to rebound above $70,000 as markets stabilized.</p>
<p>By Feb. 9, Bitcoin is bouncing again, proving it remains a high-beta gauge of global liquidity sentiment.</p>
<h2>Four scenarios for traders watching the China–yields–BTC feedback loop</h2>
<p>To understand what comes next, traders are not just looking at whether China sells, but also how the market absorbs those sales. The impact on Bitcoin depends entirely on the speed of the move and the resulting stress on dollar liquidity.</p>
<p>Here are the four key ways this dynamic is likely to play out in the months ahead.</p>
<ul>
<li> <strong>“Contained de-risking” (base case):</strong></li>
</ul>
<p>In this case, banks slow their incremental buying, and China’s headline holdings drift lower, mostly through maturities and reallocation rather than urgent selling.</p>
<p>As a result, US yields grind higher by 10 to 30 basis points over time, largely through term premium and the market’s need to absorb supply.</p>
<p>Here, Bitcoin faces a mild headwind, but the dominant drivers remain US macro data and shifting expectations for the Federal Reserve.</p>
<ul>
<li><strong>“Term premium reprices” (bearish macro regime): </strong></li>
</ul>
<p>If the market interprets China’s guidance as a secular shift in foreign appetite, yields could reprice into the Kansas City Fed’s 25–100 basis point range.</p>
<p>A move like that, especially if real yields lead, would likely tighten financial conditions enough to compress risk exposure and push crypto lower through higher funding costs, reduced liquidity, and risk-parity-style deleveraging.</p>
<ul>
<li><strong>“Disorderly liquidity shock” (tail risk): </strong></li>
</ul>
<p>A fast, politicized, or crowded exit, even if not led by China, can create outsized price effects.</p>
<p>The stress-episode framework linking a $100 billion foreign-official sale to a more than 100-basis-point move on impact is the kind of reference traders cite when considering nonlinear outcomes.</p>

<p>The difference is that one of these moves gets called a dump, and the other gets called background noise, because the paper in your wallet still says one dollar.</p>
