<h2>The dollar isn't worth a dollar anymore</h2>
<p>The scrumpled-up dollar you recently found in an old jacket you haven't worn in three years feels the same, but trust me, it's not. If you're struggling to understand this, Frank Reynolds has a great <a href="https://youtu.be/ohsoyoXLfYA?si=3OnlaWC8CVYy4AgM&amp;t=152">explanation</a>.</p>
<p><br />
Jokes aside, if you want the cleanest version of why, you start with purchasing power.</p>
<p>The Bureau of Labor Statistics CPI-U index, not seasonally adjusted, was 300.840 in Feb 2023, according to the <a href="https://www.bls.gov/news.release/archives/cpi_03142023.pdf">BLS</a>.</p>
<p>The latest complete CPI-U print we have as of now is Dec 2025 at 324.054 on <a href="https://fred.stlouisfed.org/series/CPIAUCNS">FRED</a>. That is the slow part of the loss, the part you do not feel on any single morning.</p>
<p>Do the math, 300.840 divided by 324.054, and the Feb 2023 dollar has about 92.8 cents of purchasing power by Dec 2025, before you even bring foreign exchange into it.</p>
<p>Now layer the dollar’s external value on top, since the whole point of DXY-style talk is that the world prices you in real time.</p>
<p>The chart shows a roughly 4.56% drop in DXY over the three-year window, and using that FX leg with the CPI leg is how you get the “my dollar is really 88.7 cents” gut punch.</p>
<p>0.955 times 0.928 lands around 0.887, call it 88.7 cents, and that is before you make the more complicated argument about how people experience inflation unevenly, depending on what they buy.</p>
<figure class="wp-caption aligncenter" id="attachment_518949" style="width: 1024px;"><img alt="Dollar performance over the last 3 years" class="wp-image-518949 size-large" height="719" src="https://cryptoslate.com/wp-content/uploads/2026/02/Screenshot-2026-02-09-at-13.33.48-1024x719.png" width="1024" /><figcaption class="wp-caption-text" id="caption-attachment-518949">Dollar performance over the last 3 years</figcaption></figure>
<p>There is a more conservative way to do the same comparison, and it matters because critics will try to poke holes in the index we choose.</p>
<p>The broad trade-weighted dollar index, DTWEXBGS on <a href="https://fred.stlouisfed.org/series/DTWEXBGS/">FRED</a>, is close to flat over the comparable window, it nudges the composite “cash reality” toward about 92.5 cents instead of 88.7.</p>
<p>So, at the very least we can put it within that range, and it is hard to argue with, your $1 bill is still a $1 bill, and in real terms it buys something closer to $0.89 to $0.93 of what it used to, depending on whether you use DXY or a broad trade-weighted basket.</p>
<p>That is the baseline, and it has nothing to do with crypto, it is just the quiet math of living through time.</p>

<h2>And then there is Bitcoin.</h2>
<p>On Feb 3, 2023, BTC was around $23,424. Using that starting point offers a perspective everyone forgets d|https://cryptoslate.com/your-cash-fell-to-88-cents-on-the-dollar-while-bitcoin-is-up-to-3-26-if-your-bought-before-the-crash/|etf,regulation,macro,defi,selloff|BTC,ETH,LINK,DOT,NEAR|negative|1.0|1770720435898
cryptoslate_1770661519000_2187207|1770661519000|2026|2|7|2026-02-09|cryptoslate|Crypto market bottom is closer than you think as Bitcoin miner reserves crash to historic lows|<p>Bitcoin’s price story lately has been told like it only has one main character, the ETFs.</p>
<p>Money goes in, price goes up, money goes out, price goes down. It’s a clean narrative, and it’s not wrong, but it’s incomplete, because Bitcoin is not just a ticker. The network has its own internal plumbing, and some of the best clues about where we are in the cycle are sitting in plain sight on-chain.</p>
<p>The charts I’ve been watching feel a bit like checking the pulse under the headline. Miners, long-term holders, and the broad mass of wallets don’t react the way ETFs do, they don’t flip direction on a whim, they grind, they hold, then they crack, then they recover.</p>
<p>That is why I decided to check in on a few cycle gauges that have kept me honest across the years, miner reserves, NUPL, and the percentage of UTXOs in profit.</p>
<h2>Bitcoin miner reserves dwindle</h2>
<p>We'll start with miners, because miners are where the <a href="https://cryptoslate.com/coins/bitcoin">Bitcoin</a> “real economy” meets the fiat world. They have bills to pay, they are constantly converting electricity into BTC, and when the math stops working they don’t get to be philosophical about it, they sell, they shut down, they restructure, they move, they hedge, they survive.</p>
<p>In the data here, miner reserves are sliding to levels we haven’t seen since the early era. Miners currently hold about 1.801 million BTC.</p>
<figure class="wp-caption aligncenter" id="attachment_518918" style="width: 1024px;"><img alt="Bitcoin miner reserves have steadily declined from their early-cycle peak, even as price trends higher over the long term, underscoring a structural drawdown in miner-held supply. (Source: CryptoQuant)" class="wp-image-518918 size-large" height="576" src="https://cryptoslate.com/wp-content/uploads/2026/02/Bitcoin-Miner-Reserve-All-Miners-1-1024x576.png" width="1024" /><figcaption class="wp-caption-text" id="caption-attachment-518918">Bitcoin miner reserves have steadily declined from their early-cycle peak, even as price trends higher over the long term, underscoring a structural drawdown in miner-held supply. (Source: CryptoQuant)</figcaption></figure>
<p>Over the last 60 days, they’ve shed roughly 6,300 BTC, just over 100 BTC per day on average. That is a steady leak, the kind you see when the business is under pressure, and the treasury becomes working capital.</p>
<figure class="wp-caption aligncenter" id="attachment_518919" style="width: 1024px;"><img alt="Bitcoin miner reserves continue to trend lower through 2024–2026, even as price experiences sharp rallies and pullbacks, highlighting persistent balance sheet pressure across the mining sector. (Source: CryptoQuant)" class="wp-image-518919 size-large" height="576" src="https://cryptoslate.com/wp-content/uploads/2026/02/Bitcoin-Miner-Reserve-All-Miners-1024x576.png" width="1024" /><figcaption class="wp-caption-text" id="caption-attachment-518919">Bitcoin miner reserves continue to trend lower through 2024–2026, even as price experiences sharp rallies and pullbacks, highlighting persistent balance sheet pressure across the mining sector. (Source: CryptoQuant)</figcaption></figure>
<p>In dollar terms, the picture gets more dramatic. Miner reserves in USD are around $133 billion, down a little over 20 percent in about two months. Some of that is price, some of that is coins leaving miner wallets, and the combination is what matters, because it tightens their margin of safety.</p>
<p>If BTC is falling while reserves are thinning, miners have less cushion to ride out volatility, and the market has one more source of potential supply if things get ugly.</p>
<figure class="wp-caption aligncenter" id="attachment_518920" style="width: 1024px;"><img alt="Bitcoin miner reserves measured in USD have dropped sharply alongside recent price weakness, erasing a significant portion of the sector’s balance-sheet buffer despite remaining elevated by historical standards. (Source: CryptoQuant)" class="wp-image-518920 size-large" height="576" src="https://cryptoslate.com/wp-content/uploads/2026/02/Bitcoin-Miner-Reserve-USD-All-Miners-1024x576.png" width="1024" /><figcaption class="wp-caption-text" id="caption-attachment-518920">Bitcoin miner reserves measured in USD have dropped sharply alongside recent price weakness, erasing a significant portion of the sector’s balance-sheet buffer despite remaining elevated by historical standards. (Source: CryptoQuant)</figcaption></figure>
<p>This is where the ETF narrative collides with the on-chain narrative. The ETF tape can be brutal, and it can overwhelm everything else in the short run.</p>
<p>Looking at recent flow data, the net move over roughly the last 10 trading days shown is about negative $1.7 billion, around $170 million per day on average. That number matters because it’s big enough to dominate marginal demand, and it’s fast enough to change sentiment before most people even register the shift.</p>
<p>But the problem with staring at flows alone is that it tells you what’s happening at the surface, not what’s building underneath.</p>
<h2>Net unrealized profit and loss chart</h2>
<p>If I’m trying to work out where we are in the cycle, I want to know whether the market is in a normal downturn that can snap back, or whether it’s approaching a deeper reset that needs a real washout.</p>
<p>That’s why I keep one eye on NUPL, net unrealized profit and loss. It’s not perfect, nothing is, but it does a good job of showing when the market as a whole is sitting on profit, sitting on pain, or sitting somewhere in between.</p>
<p>In the latest data, NUPL is still positive, around 0.215, which keeps Bitcoin in the green zone. It has fallen hard over the last couple of months, down about 0.17, and that slope is the part that grabs me, because you can feel the mood shifting in that compression.</p>
<figure class="wp-caption aligncenter" id="attachment_518917" style="width: 1024px;"><img alt="Bitcoin’s Net Unrealized Profit/Loss (NUPL) remains positive but has compressed sharply, signaling declining aggregate profitability without a full capitulation into net losses. (Source: CryptoQuant)" class="wp-image-518917 size-large" height="576" src="https://cryptoslate.com/wp-content/uploads/2026/02/Bitcoin-Net-Unrealized-Profit_Loss-NUPL-1024x576.png" width="1024" /><figcaption class="wp-caption-text" id="caption-attachment-518917">Bitcoin’s Net Unrealized Profit/Loss (NUPL) remains positive but has compressed sharply, signaling declining aggregate profitability without a full capitulation into net losses. (Source: CryptoQuant)</figcaption></figure>
<p>The line in the sand for me is when NUPL goes below zero, and especially if it pushes toward negative 0.2.</p>
<p>NUPL last dipped below zero in early 2023, and the last time it was below negative 0.2 was late 2022. That’s the territory where true capitulation lives, that’s where the “bear bottom confirmation” argument has usually been strongest.</p>
<p>We aren’t there right now, and that matters if you’re trying to call a bottom today. It doesn’t mean we cannot be close, it does mean we don’t yet have the kind of confirmation that usually comes with a classic cycle low.</p>
<h2>How many trades are in profit right now?</h2>
<p>Then there’s the UTXOs in profit chart, and this one is quietly fascinating because it shows how the market has matured over time. At the bottoms in earlier cycles, almost nobody was in profit.</p>
<p>In 2011 the trough was around 8 percent, in 2015 around 15 percent, in 2018 around 49 percent. The COVID crash in 2020 is a weird outlier that I tend to treat as its own event.</p>
<p>In 2023, the trough was about 60 percent. In the current data, 2026 has already printed a low around 58 percent, and the latest reading is around 71 percent.</p>
<p>That pattern, those rising floor levels, tells a human story. <h2>Stablecoin “yield” and the bank-deposit fight</h2>
<p>The yield dispute is tied to product economics that are already visible in consumer offers. Coinbase advertises “3.50% rewards on USDC” as part of Coinbase One, while <a href="https://www.coinbase.com/usdc/">disclosing</a> that the rewards rate is subject to change and can vary by region.</p>
<p>Those caveats make “yield” less a protocol-level feature than a distribution decision and a compliance choice. The policy argument turns on whether payouts are treated as a rebate or loyalty benefit, a bank-like interest substitute, or a yield product that draws securities-style scrutiny.</p>
<p>The Wall Street Journal, <a href="https://www.wsj.com/finance/regulation/banks-and-crypto-clash-over-tokens-that-pay-more-than-deposits-c9159c0e">describing</a> the bank-crypto clash over these products, contrasted stablecoin rewards around 3.5% with bank deposit rates around 0.1%. It also reported that the Treasury had estimated a potential $6.6 trillion drawdown in deposits under certain assumptions, a figure best treated as a scenario output rather than an observed flow.</p>
<p>Bloomberg Law’s reporting described the issue as unresolved even after the White House convened stakeholders. Related: <em>CryptoSlate’s</em> prior coverage of <a href="https://cryptoslate.com/coinbase-to-halt-usdc-earn-program-on-mica-compliant-regions/">USDC rewards changes under MiCA-aligned rules</a>.</p>

<h2>What the CLARITY Act text does on custody and DeFi</h2>
<p>The legislative vehicle at the center of the debate is H.R. 3633, which <a href="https://www.congress.gov/bill/119th-congress/house-bill/3633">passed</a> the House and was sent to the Senate, where it was received and referred to the Senate Banking Committee on Sept. 18, 2025.</p>
<p>The bill text <a href="https://www.congress.gov/bill/119th-congress/house-bill/3633/text">includes</a> an explicit “Protection of Self-Custody” clause. It states consumers retain the right to maintain hardware or software wallets and to engage in direct peer-to-peer transactions, language that becomes a measuring stick for whether a final compromise protects retail custody choices while regulating intermediaries.</p>
<p>The House text also includes headings that carve out “DECENTRALIZED FINANCE ACTIVITIES NOT SUBJECT TO THIS ACT” in amendment sections touching both the Se|https://cryptoslate.com/white-house-meeting-can-unfreeze-the-clarity-act-this-week-but-crypto-rewards-liklely-to-be-the-price/|regulation,defi,exchange|ETH,SOL,LINK,DOT,NEAR,MKR|negative|0.65|1770720435900
cryptoslate_1770606928000_162798|1770606928000|2026|2|6|2026-02-08|cryptoslate|Bitcoin bears could sleepwalk into a $8.65 billion trap as options max pain expiry nears $90,000|<p><a href="https://cryptoslate.com/coins/bitcoin/">Bitcoin’s</a> next big options gravity well sits on Mar. 27 (260327), and the reason is simple: this is where the market has parked a thick stack of conditional bets that will need to be unwound, rolled forward, or paid out as the clock runs down.</p>
<p>The Mar. 27 expiry carries about $8.65B in notional OI and flags $90,000 as max pain, a rough reference point for where, in aggregate, option holders would feel the most pain at settlement.</p>
<p>The broader options complex is enormous, with total BTC options open interest around $31.99B across exchanges, led by <a href="https://cryptoslate.com/companies/deribit/">Deribit</a> at roughly $25.56B, with the rest split across <a href="https://cryptoslate.com/companies/cme-group/">CME</a>, <a href="https://cryptoslate.com/companies/okx/">OKX</a>, <a href="https://cryptoslate.com/companies/binance/">Binance</a>, and <a href="https://cryptoslate.com/companies/bybit/">Bybit</a>.</p>
<figure class="wp-caption aligncenter" id="attachment_518808" style="width: 1258px;"><img alt="bitcoin options open interest" class="size-full wp-image-518808" height="466" src="https://cryptoslate.com/wp-content/uploads/2026/02/Screenshot-2026-02-06-at-22.46.27.png" width="1258" /><figcaption class="wp-caption-text" id="caption-attachment-518808">Chart showing Bitcoin options open interest from Feb.1 to Feb. 5, 2026 (Source: <a href="https://www.coinglass.com/pro/options/OpenInterest">CoinGlass</a>)</figcaption></figure>
<p>That concentration can shape how price behaves on the way there, particularly when liquidity thins and hedging flows start to matter more than anyone wants to admit.</p>
<p>Options can often sound like some kind of private language of institutional traders, which is convenient right up until they start influencing spot price. Our goal here is to translate a crowded derivatives calendar into something legible: where the bets are concentrated, how that concentration can change behavior in spot markets, and why March 27 stands out.</p>

<div class="cs-article-embed">
    <a class="cs-article-embed__link" href="https://cryptoslate.com/why-im-bullish-that-my-49k-bitcoin-prediction-is-on-track-as-btc-closes-in-on-major-buy-zone/">

<h2>March 27 and the shape of the bets</h2>
<p>On Mar. 27 (260327), data shows more calls than puts, roughly 69.85K calls versus 53.25K puts, with puts carrying far more market value than calls in that moment.</p>
<figure class="wp-caption aligncenter" id="attachment_518804" style="width: 1258px;"><img alt="bitcoin options OI by expiry" class="size-full wp-image-518804" height="466" src="https://cryptoslate.com/wp-content/uploads/2026/02/Screenshot-2026-02-06-at-22.41.56.png" width="1258" /><figcaption class="wp-caption-text" id="caption-attachment-518804">Chart showing the open interest for Bitcoin options on Deribit by expiry on Feb. 6, 2026 (Source: <a href="https://www.coinglass.com/pro/options/OIExpiry">CoinGlass</a>)</figcaption></figure>
<p>That combination might look strange and even contradictory, until you translate it into everyday incentives.</p>
<p>Calls can be plentiful because they offer defined-risk upside exposure that feels emotionally painless to hold, while puts can be more expensive because downside protection is often bought closer to where it actually hurts, and it tends to get repriced more aggressively when the market is nervous.</p>
<p>The volume data adds a second clue about what was happening at the margin. For the same Mar. 27 expiry, CoinGlass data shows puts around 17.98K versus calls around 10.46K in trading volume, again with puts carrying the heavier market value.</p>
<figure class="wp-caption aligncenter" id="attachment_518807" style="width: 1258px;"><img alt="bitcoin options volume by expiry" class="wp-image-518807 size-full" height="466" src="https://cryptoslate.com/wp-content/uploads/2026/02/Screenshot-2026-02-06-at-22.43.27.png" width="1258" /><figcaption class="wp-caption-text" id="caption-attachment-518807">Chart showing the trading volume for Bitcoin options on Deribit by expiry on Feb. 6, 2026 (Source: CoinGlass)</figcaption></figure>
<p>That tells us the flow that day leans more toward paying for protection than chasing upside, even while the outstanding inventory still looks call-heavy on count.</p>
<p>Now place that against spot and the broader pile.</p>
<p>March can feel far away in calendar terms, especially when the market is this volatile, but in options terms, it's close enough to exert gravity once nearer expiries finish shuffling positions forward.</p>
<p>When one date holds several billion in notional, it becomes a focal point for rolling, hedging, and all of the other quiet mechanical work market makers do to stay roughly neutral as customers buy and sell convexity. While this doesn't guarantee a particular price, it does increase the odds of price behaving as if there are invisible grooves in the road, because in a derivatives-heavy market, hedging flows can add friction in some ranges and remove it in others.</p>
<p>That brings us to max pain. It's a bookkeeping-style calculation across strikes, not a law of nature and not a trading signal with a motor attached.</p>
<p>It can be a useful reference in the way a median can be useful, as a single marker that tells you something about the distribution, but it's blunt, and blunt tools are almost never the ones moving price.</p>
<p>What tends to matter more is where positions are crowded by strike, because crowding changes how much hedging needs to happen when spot moves. CoinGlass data shows a put/call ratio around 0.44, one more hint that the distribution is lopsided rather than smooth, and lopsided is the whole point because it's how a date stops being a calendar fact and becomes a market event.</p>
<p>There's a simple, non-trader way to hold all of this without turning it into fortune-telling.</p>
<p>As March approaches, crowded strikes can behave like zones where price movement feels oddly damped, then oddly jumpy, because the hedging response is not steady.</p>
<p>If Bitcoin wanders into a heavily populated region, the market’s automatic risk management can reinforce a range, and if Bitcoin moves hard enough to escape it, those same mechanics can flip into something that amplifies momentum instead of resisting it.</p>

cryptoslate_1770600719000_6819574|1770600719000|2026|2|6|2026-02-08|cryptoslate|Bitcoin ETF flow numbers are fundamentally broken and most traders are missing the specific sign of a crash|<p>On Jan.30, 2026, US spot <a href="https://cryptoslate.com/coins/bitcoin/">Bitcoin</a> ETFs saw $509.7 million in net <a href="https://farside.co.uk/btc/">outflows</a>, which looks like pretty straightforward negative sentiment until you look at the individual tickers and realize a few of them stayed green.</p>
<p>That contradiction aged fast over the next few days. Feb. 2 snapped back with $561.8 million in net inflows, then Feb. 3 flipped to -$272.0 million, and Feb. 4 sank to -$544.9 million. The totals went up and down, but the more useful clue was the same one hiding in plain sight on Jan. 30: the category can look like one trade from a distance, while the money inside it moves in very different rhythms.</p>
<p>By the time Bitcoin <a href="https://cryptoslate.com/bitcoin-bear-market-ends-when-three-signals-flip-and-one-is-already-starting-to-twitch/">slid below</a> $71,000, ETF flows and price finally started to rhyme.</p>
<p>If you're trying to read the ETF flow table like a mood ring, the table will definitely mislead you. The total number you see in the table is a scoreboard, not the play-by-play, and it can easily be dragged around by one large exit even while smaller pockets of demand keep persisting. The green islands in the deep red sea are real, but it's rarely the heroic resistance signal people want it to be.</p>

<div class="cs-article-embed">
    <a class="cs-article-embed__link" href="https://cryptoslate.com/bitcoin-bear-market-ends-when-three-signals-flip-and-one-is-already-starting-to-twitch/">

<h2>Why &#8220;total flows&#8221; lie on the days you care most about</h2>
<p>Secondary-market trading is people swapping ETF shares with each other, while primary-market creations and redemptions are what change the share count. Flow tables almost always aim at the second layer, the net creation or destruction of shares. The SEC’s <a href="https://www.sec.gov/investor/alerts/etfs.pdf">investor bulletin</a> makes the key distinction very clear: ETF shares trade on an exchange, but supply changes through the creation and redemption process.</p>
<p>That split matters because a day can see crazy volumes and price action and still print zero flows for a given fund if buyers and sellers just match each other in the secondary market. And a day can print a huge outflow because one or a few large holders decide to redeem, even if there's steady buying elsewhere.</p>
<p>This is why dispersion is worth tracking. Instead of staring at the net number, count how many funds are green versus red, then ask how concentrated the red is. On Jan. 30, the numbers were brutal everywhere: <a href="https://cryptoslate.com/products/ishares-bitcoin-trust/">IBIT</a> -$528.3 million versus a -$509.7 million total, which means the rest of the complex was slightly positive when you add it up. <a href="https://cryptoslate.com/products/fidelity-wise-origin-bitcoin-trust/">FBTC's</a> $7.3 million, <a href="https://cryptoslate.com/products/ark-21shares-bitcoin-etf/">ARKB's</a> $8.3 million, and <a href="https://cryptoslate.com/products/valkyrie-bitcoin-fund/">BRRR's</a> $3 million inflows were small, but they were still inflows.</p>
<p>At the beginning of February, we saw a much cleaner example of what broad-based demand looks like and what a <a href="https://cryptoslate.com/bitcoin-supply-guide-a-simple-dashboard-for-btc-supply-shows-when-holders-sell-miners-strain-and-etfs-add-pressure/">concentrated exit</a> looks like.</p>
<p>On Feb. 2, net inflows were spread across the leaders, including IBIT's $142.0 million and <a href="https://cryptoslate.com/products/fidelity-wise-origin-bitcoin-trust/">FBTC's</a> $153.3 million, <a href="https://cryptoslate.com/products/bitwise-bitcoin-etf/">BITB's</a> $96.5 million, and ARKB's $65.1 million inflows joining in. That's what a category-wide &#8220;buy day&#8221; looks like in the flow data: more than one desk, more than one platform, and more than one fund.</p>
<p>On Feb. 3, the table turned into a lesson in internal conflict. IBIT was still up $60.0 million, while FBTC printed -$148.7 million and ARKB -$62.5 million, pulling the total to -$272.0 million. The category was net red while the biggest vehicle stayed green, which is the mirror image of Jan. 30’s story. The takeaway here is not that one ticker smart money and the others aren't, but that the ETF market now has different buyer types with different rules, and they don't all hit the button at the same time.</p>
<p>On Feb. 4, the outflows deepened to -$544.9 million, with IBIT -$373.4 million and FBTC -$86.4 million leading the day, plus smaller outflows across other funds. That was the day Bitcoin dipped under $72,000 in a broad risk-off backdrop.</p>
<p>When analyzing the ETF market, it's important not to treat every green print as fresh conviction. A micro-inflow can be real demand, but it can also be allocation drift getting corrected, a model portfolio topping up a sleeve, or a platform with scheduled behavior that doesn't really care what crypto Twitter is doing this week. Big totals are often driven by a much smaller number of actors than people assume, and small prints can be driven by a much larger number of small accounts than the headlines imply.</p>
<h2>The real reasons micro-inflows happen, and what February’s slump did to them</h2>
<p>The easiest explanation is the least satisfying and the most frequent: one large redemption can dominate the day. Jan. 30 was a single-ticker gravity well, with IBIT’s $528.3 million outflow overwhelming everything else. Feb. 4 did something similar, with IBIT's $373.4 million outflowdoing most of the work.</p>
<p>Next comes distribution behavior. Some funds get embedded in advisor platforms and model portfolios where allocations update on schedules, sometimes monthly, sometimes quarterly, sometimes when a portfolio crosses a risk band. That sort of demand can remain steady even when fast money is de-risking, and it can show up as small greens on days when the total looks ugly.</p>
<p>Then there's internal switching. Investors rotate between products for reasons unrelated to Bitcoin’s fundamentals: fees, familiarity with a particular issuer, operational comfort, or an institution consolidating exposure for reporting simplicity. A switch day can look like there are buyers in one fund and sellers in another, while the true story is that it's the same exposure, just with a different wrapper.</p>
<p>The Feb. 4–5 slump adds one more ingredient that makes dispersion louder: forced deleveraging in the rest of the crypto market. When the market slides quickly and liquidations pick up, desks that need to raise cash sell what they can, and that can include ETF positions.</p>
<p>That backdrop helps |https://cryptoslate.com/bitcoin-etf-flow-numbers-are-fundamentally-broken-and-most-traders-are-missing-the-specific-sign-of-a-crash/|etf,regulation,institutional,defi,whale,mining,selloff|BTC,ETH,SOL,LINK,DOT|negative|1.0|1770720435902
cryptoslate_1770591636000_9184828|1770591636000|2026|2|6|2026-02-08|cryptoslate|Do CME gaps always have to fill? Bitcoin’s $60k flush says no|<p><a href="https://cryptoslate.com/coins/bitcoin/">Bitcoin</a> trades every minute of every day, but <a href="https://cryptoslate.com/companies/cme-group/">CME</a> Bitcoin futures stop for the weekend. That mismatch is how a CME gap is born, and why it keeps turning up in the middle of the most stressful weeks.</p>
<p>A CME gap is the blank space on a CME futures chart between Friday’s final traded level and the first traded level when the market reopens Sunday evening (US time). CME futures trade on a weekly schedule with a weekend break, while spot Bitcoin keeps moving. When the first CME print lands far from Friday’s close, the chart draws a jump and leaves an empty zone in between. That zone is the gap.</p>
<p><em>CryptoSlate’s</em> <a href="https://cryptoslate.com/market-reports/whats-a-cme-gap-and-why-does-it-get-filled/">report</a> on this topic made the key point that the gap is not a mystical force, but a record of time when one market was closed, and the other was still trading. This is not about prophecy. It’s about a calendar mismatch that becomes visible on charts.</p>
<p>This week gave us a clean, real-world demo.</p>
<p>On the continuous CME Bitcoin futures chart, the Friday (Jan. 30) close printed around $84,105, and the first Sunday reopen printed near $77,730, leaving a roughly $6,375 weekend gap. Then the drawdown accelerated.</p>
<p>Bitcoin slid from about $72,999 at the start of Feb. 5 to a low of $62,181 on Coinbase, and then printed near $60,000 early Feb. 6 before rebounding into the mid $60,000s. CME’s 30-minute series shows the same shape, with a low near $60,005 and a rebound toward $66,900.</p>
<p>Even with that kind of volatility, the prior Friday level in the mid $80,000s stayed far overhead. The gap remained open through Feb. 6 because the price never got close enough to revisit it.</p>
<p>That’s a good place to start, because it answers the question most non-traders are really asking when they hear the term “gap.” They're asking why two prices that both say BTC can look like they live in different universes for a moment, and why that mismatch sometimes disappears as the week goes on.</p>
<h2>How a gap forms when one Bitcoin market takes the weekend off</h2>
<p>CME lists cash-settled Bitcoin futures that trade in a near-continuous weekly session: Sunday evening through Friday afternoon, with a daily break, and a hard weekend stop. But spot Bitcoin doesn’t have that off switch, so if a big move hits on Saturday, CME can’t print it in real time. The chart just has no data for that stretch.</p>
<p>When CME reopens, it doesn’t resume trading from the Friday close. It resumes from wherever the market is at the opening hour. If spot is down 8% or up 6% while CME was closed, the first futures trade will reflect that, plus whatever premium or discount futures carry at the reopen. The result is a visible jump, and the empty zone between Friday’s last level and Sunday’s first level becomes the gap.</p>
<figure class="wp-caption aligncenter" id="attachment_518695" style="width: 1588px;"><img alt="CME gaps bitcoin futures" class="size-full wp-image-518695" height="856" src="https://cryptoslate.com/wp-content/uploads/2026/02/CME-gaps-bitcoin-futures.png" width="1588" /><figcaption class="wp-caption-text" id="caption-attachment-518695">Graph showing Bitcoin futures on CME from Jan. 15 to Feb. 6, 2026 (Source: <a href="https://www.tradingview.com/chart/nDPOT2hW/">TradingView</a>)</figcaption></figure>
<p>The important part is what happens next, because the gap existing in the first place is a calendar fact, but the gap getting filled is market behavior.</p>
<p>Think of the gap as a skipped page in a book. Friday ends on a cliffhanger, the weekend writes three chapters somewhere else, and CME comes back with a whole new chapter. The skipped pages are still missing on the CME chart, but the story has already advanced on spot exchanges.</p>
<p>This is also why the gap meme can feel persuasive in weeks like this one. When Bitcoin is calm, the reopen is close to Friday’s close, so there is no dramatic blank space to talk about. When Bitcoin is violent, the blank space is big, and the human brain treats big blank spaces as unfinished business.</p>
<p><strong>Myth vs. reality:</strong></p>
<ul>
<li><strong>Myth: </strong>“CME gaps have to fill.”</li>
<li><strong>Reality: </strong>Gaps often fill because markets tend to converge once CME liquidity returns, but they do not <em>have</em> to fill on any schedule. In trend weeks, the gap can sit open for a long time.</li>
</ul>
<h2>Why gaps often get filled, and why this week shows the limits</h2>
<p>A &#8220;gap fill&#8221; simply means price later trades back through the empty zone, often all the way to the prior CME close. <em>CryptoSlate’s</em> explainer argued that this happens so often because, once CME is live again, there are practical incentives to pull futures and spot back toward each other.</p>
<p>That pull is just a set of boring, repeatable reasons that tend to show up during staffed market hours.</p>
<p>If futures and spot are far apart, there’s money to be made in narrowing the difference. Companies that can access both markets can buy low and sell high, aiming to profit as the spread compresses.</p>
<p>This is a convergence process driven by arbitrage and relative-value positioning rather than a belief that Bitcoin must go up or down. You can understand the intuition without touching the trade, because two linked markets rarely tolerate a huge disagreement for long once liquidity is back, and risk limits are active.</p>
<p>Then there’s the attention effect. Gaps are now widely tracked and shared, which emphasizes their importance during price volatility. When lots of people watch the same level, liquidity tends to gather there. That liquidity can make it easier for the price to revisit the area, especially in choppy markets where mean reversion is already in play.</p>
<p><em>CryptoSlate’s</em> previous report backed the claim that gaps fill with numbers from its own study, showing a high fill rate and a tendency for many fills to happen quickly once CME sessions resume. That helps explain why the gap myth survives: it has enough historical reinforcement to feel like a rule, even though it isn’t one.</p>
<p>This is where Feb. 5 and Feb. 6 matter, because they show the boundary case that keeps the story honest.</p>
<p>Bitcoin dropped hard, touched $60,000, and then snapped back, causing over $1 billion in liquidations in just 24 hours.</p>
<p>That is the kind of environment where the CME gap starts mattering less. When the market is dumping and leverage is being forced out, price doesn’t care about a few missing candles in CME’s chart from the week before. It cares about where bids actually exist right now.</p>
<p>Both Coinbase and CME fell into the low $60,000s, then bounced toward the mid $60,000s. So, the old CME Friday close near $84,105 stopped being a magnet for price and started looking more like a distant marker.</p>
<p>This is also why the open gap can be a better explaining tool than predicting one.</p>
<p>In a calm market, fills can happen quickly because the price is already oscillating and liquidity is comfortable revisiting prior levels.</p>
<p>In a stressed market, the open gap is a reminder that the price has moved so far that the old close is simply out of reach in the near term. That’s not a failure of the concept; it’s just the concept doing its job: showing the consequences of a weekend move that never got retraced.</p>
<p>The Feb. 6 coverage of corporate Bitcoin treasuries adds a second layer that makes the story feel bigger than chart culture. <em>CryptoSlate</em> <a href="https://cryptoslate.com/as-bitcoin-sinks-to-60k-btc-treasury-companies-go-10-billion-underwater-and-one-major-firm-is-bracing-for-a-27-billion-disaster/?utm_source=chatgpt.com">reported</a> that the slide toward $60,000 pushed corporate holders deeper underwater on paper, and it singled o|https://cryptoslate.com/do-cme-gaps-always-have-to-fill-bitcoins-60k-flush-says-no/|regulation,macro,exchange,selloff|BTC,ETH,LINK,MATIC,NEAR,TRX|negative|0.95|1770720435903
cryptoslate_1770581725000_162995|1770581725000|2026|2|6|2026-02-08|cryptoslate|Bitcoin must recover $71,500 soon or the drift back to $60,000 begins|<h2>Bitcoin keeps knocking on $71,500, sooner or later the door opens</h2>
<p>Bitcoin made a familiar but stressful move this week; it bounced hard enough to make the skeptics quiet and the dip buyers loud again.</p>
<p>After the crash down to around $60,000, the price clawed its way back to the a spot that has become the center of gravity, the $71,500 zone.</p>

<p>Each time, the market hesitated, traders leaned in, and the rally ran out of oxygen. Now Bitcoin is back around $70,900, it looks like it wants to test $71,500 again, and this is the moment worth paying attention to, even if you don’t trade, even if you only check the price once a week.</p>
<p>Because some levels are more like shared memories than simple numbers on a screen.</p>
<p>$71,500 is one of those.</p>
<figure class="wp-caption aligncenter" id="attachment_518883" style="width: 1024px;"><img alt="Bitcoin's attempt to retake $71,500" class="wp-image-518883 size-large" height="571" src="https://cryptoslate.com/wp-content/uploads/2026/02/Screenshot-2026-02-08-at-12.57.18-1024x571.png" width="1024" /><figcaption class="wp-caption-text" id="caption-attachment-518883">Bitcoin's attempt to retake $71,500</figcaption></figure>
<h2>Why $71,500 keeps showing up</h2>
<p>When a level gets tested again and again, it becomes a kind of public square.</p>
<p>Everyone sees it on their chart. But not everyone discusses it in group chats or has a plan for it.</p>
<p>That matters because Bitcoin is a market that runs on emotion as much as math.</p>
<p>When price approaches a level like $71,500 after a violent drop, you get a mix of people who want out, people who want in, and people who want confirmation. That creates friction, and friction creates the stalling you can see on the chart.</p>
<p>For traders, this is where decisions get made quickly, stops get placed tightly, and leverage gets bold.</p>
<p>For long-term holders, this is where the story gets rewritten. A market that couldn’t get above $71,500 starts to feel weak, a market that reclaims it starts to feel repaired.</p>
<p>That difference in feeling is why the zone matters.</p>
<h2>The lines on my chart are not decoration</h2>
<p>The horizontal lines in the chart are the top and bottom of channels I’ve tracked over the <a href="https://cryptoslate.com/bitcoin-channel-predictions-align-with-market-movements-over-6-months/">last two years. </a></p>
<figure class="wp-caption aligncenter" id="attachment_518882" style="width: 1024px;"><img alt="Bitcoin price action and channels over the last week" class="wp-image-518882 size-large" height="573" src="https://cryptoslate.com/wp-content/uploads/2026/02/Screenshot-2026-02-08-at-12.56.44-1024x573.png" width="1024" /><figcaption class="wp-caption-text" id="caption-attachment-518882">Bitcoin price action and channels over the last week</figcaption></figure>
<p>They are areas where Bitcoin has repeatedly found support or slammed into resistance. They are built from a blend of historical leverage behavior, order-book dynamics, psychological price levels, and the familiar entry and exit points many traders use when trading with size.</p>
<p>I’m not pretending this is a magic formula, it’s a map. It gives me a way to stop guessing and start planning.</p>
<p>And right now, that map says $71,500 is the next major checkpoint.</p>
<p>If you’ve been following my work this cycle, you’ll recognize the theme. I’ve spent months writing about how cycle highs form, how risk leaks out of the system, and how bear markets often feel obvious in hindsight but rarely feel obvious in the moment.</p>

beincrypto_1770739480000_8093850|1770739480000|2026|2|7|2026-02-10|beincrypto|Ethereum To Make the Most Transformative Architectural Leap Since The Merge.|<p><strong>Tomorrow, February 11, 2026, the first L1-zkEVM workshop will give a first look at a new system that could make block validation faster, cheaper, and more accessible for everyone.</strong></p>



<p>Instead of re-executing every transaction in a block, Ethereum may soon rely on zero-knowledge (ZK) proofs, enabling validators to verify correctness through cryptographic proofs.</p>



<h2 class="bic-gutenberg-heading wp-heading wp-block-heading" id="h-why-ethereum-s-shift-to-zk-proofs-could-redefine-block-validation">Why Ethereum&rsquo;s Shift to ZK Proofs Could Redefine Block Validation</h2>



<p>Ethereum Foundation researcher Ladislaus.eth called it &ldquo;arguably one of the more consequential&rdquo; upgrades in the network&rsquo;s history.</p>



<figure class="wp-block-embed is-type-rich is-provider-twitter wp-block-embed-twitter"><div class="wp-block-embed__wrapper">
<blockquote class="twitter-tweet"><p dir="ltr" lang="zxx"><a href="https://t.co/TwylcccdzB">https://t.co/TwylcccdzB</a></p>&mdash; ladislaus.eth (@ladislaus0x) <a href="https://twitter.com/ladislaus0x/status/2020874834855514278?ref_src=twsrc%5Etfw">February 9, 2026</a></blockquote>
</div></figure>



<p>The change is part of the <a href="https://ethereum-magicians.org/t/l1-zkevm-roadmap-2026-integrating-zkevm-proofs-into-ethereums-core-protocol/27595" rel="noreferrer noopener nofollow" target="_blank">L1-zkEVM 2026 roadmap</a> and focuses on the EIP-8025 (Optional Execution Proofs) feature. This allows certain validators, called zkAttesters, to confirm blocks using cryptographic proofs instead of checking every transaction themselves.</p>



<p>The shift is optional, meaning no one is forced to upgrade, and all existing nodes continue to work as they do today. However, for those who adopt it, the benefits may be significant.</p>



<blockquote class="max-w-xl text-4.5 border-l-2 border-blue-600 pl-11 mb-9 select-all [&amp;_p]:!mb-0 wp-block-quote is-layout-flow wp-block-quote-is-layout-flow">
<p>&ldquo;The first L1-zkEVM breakout call is scheduled for February 11, 2026, 15:00 UTC,&rdquo; <a href="https://x.com/ladislaus0x/status/2020874834855514278" rel="noreferrer noopener nofollow" target="_blank">wrote</a> Ladislaus.eth.</p>
</blockquote>



<p>Today, validating a block requires re-executing every transaction, which takes more time and resources as the network grows.</p>



<p>ZK proofs enable zkAttesters to verify a block almost instantly without storing the entire blockchain.</p>



<p>This is not just about speed. By lowering the hardware, storage, and bandwidth requirements, Ethereum becomes far more accessible.</p>



<p>Solo stakers and home validators can participate fully using regular consumer hardware. This keeps the network decentralized and true to the &ldquo;don&rsquo;t trust, verify&rdquo; philosophy.</p>



<figure class="wp-block-embed is-type-rich is-provider-twitter wp-block-embed-twitter"><div class="wp-block-embed__wrapper">
<blockquote class="twitter-tweet"><p dir="ltr" lang="en">"Don't trust, verify" on consumer hardware.<br /><br />That's the whole thesis. ZK proofs replacing re-execution means Ethereum can scale gas limits without pushing solo stakers out.<br /><br />EIP-8025 being optional is the right move &ndash; upgrade paths that don't force forks are how you ship safely.</p>&mdash; The Book of Ethereum &#128216; (@Bookof_Eth) <a href="https://twitter.com/Bookof_Eth/status/2020882465317884032?ref_src=twsrc%5Etfw">February 9, 2026</a></blockquote>
</div></figure>



<p>Higher <a href="https://beincrypto.com/buterin-ethereum-l1-gas-limits-l2-future/" rel="noreferrer noopener" target="_blank">gas limits</a> and faster execution can also be achieved without pushing smaller participants out of the system.</p>



<p>EIP-8025 emphasizes flexibility and security. Proofs from multiple clients are shared across the network, and validators accept a block once enough independent proofs have been verified (currently proposed to be three out of five).</p>



<p>This approach preserves diversity among client software while keeping the network safe, inclusive, and resistant to centralization.</p>



<h2 class="bic-gutenberg-heading wp-heading wp-block-heading" id="h-institutional-momentum-and-tomorrow-s-workshop-signal-a-new-era-for-ethereum-validation">Institutional Momentum and Tomorrow&rsquo;s Workshop Signal a New Era for Ethereum Validation</h2>



<p>The timing could not be more relevant. Ethereum&rsquo;s institutional adoption is surging in 2026, with Fidelity Digital Assets, <a href="https://beincrypto.com/morgan-stanley-bitcoin-etf-crypto-adoption/" rel="noreferrer noopener" target="_blank">Morgan Stanley</a>, Grayscale, BlackRock, and <a href="https://beincrypto.com/standard-chartered-solana-price-window/" rel="noreferrer noopener" target="_blank">Standard Chartered</a> actively building or investing in the network.</p>



<blockquote class="max-w-xl text-4.5 border-l-2 border-blue-600 pl-11 mb-9 select-all [&amp;_p]:!mb-0 wp-block-quote is-layout-flow wp-block-quote-is-layout-flow">
<p>&ldquo;2026 is off to a fast start on Ethereum&hellip;One month in. Should be a fun year,&rdquo; <a href="https://x.com/davwals/status/2020915224837226584" rel="noreferrer noopener nofollow" target="_blank">remarked</a> David Walsh, head of enterprise at the Ethereum Foundation.</p>
</blockquote>



<p>Tokenized assets, stablecoins, and staking products continue to expand, while projects like the Glamsterdam hard fork (featuring enshrined proposer-builder separation, ePBS) support the practical implementation of ZK proof generation on L1.</p>



<p>L1-zkEVM development also benefits <a href="https://beincrypto.com/vitalik-buterin-ethereum-layer-2-user-decline/" rel="noreferrer noopener" target="_blank">Layer 2 rollups</a> and zkVM vendors such as ZisK, openVM, and RISC Zero, who are already proving Ethereum blocks today. Standardizing the execution witness and ZK VM APIs creates shared infrastructure, enabling both L1 validators and L2 protocols to leverage the same proofs.</p>



<p>The February 11 workshop will cover six core sub-themes:</p>



<ul class="bic-gutenberg-list wp-list list-disc ">
<li>Execution witness and guest program standardization</li>



<li>zkVM-guest API standardization</li>



<li>Consensus layer integration</li>



<li>Prover infrastructure</li>



<li>Benchmarking, and</li>



<li>Formal verification for security.</li>
</ul>



<p>It marks the official kickoff of Ethereum&rsquo;s 2026 roadmap to make block validation optional, proof-driven, and far more efficient.</p>



<figure class="wp-block-embed is-type-rich is-provider-twitter wp-block-embed-twitter"><div class="wp-block-embed__wrapper">
<blockquote class="twitter-tweet"><p dir="ltr" lang="en">Tomasz gently frontran us &#128578;  but here's our summary for how we plan to implement the L1-zkEVM roadmap: <a href="https://t.co/ioGSO8HVpr">https://t.co/ioGSO8HVpr</a><br /><br />Let us know what you think and also feel free to join the discussions on <a href="https://twitter.com/hashtag/l1?src=hash&amp;ref_src=twsrc%5Etfw">#l1</a>-zkevm &amp; <a href="https://twitter.com/hashtag/l1?src=hash&amp;ref_src=twsrc%5Etfw">#l1</a>-zkevm-protocol on the ETH R&amp;D discord server! <a href="https://t.co/C60wUGdsWl">https://t.co/C60wUGdsWl</a></p>&mdash; Kev (@kevaundray) <a href="https://twitter.com/kevaundray/status/2015813546752221348?ref_src=twsrc%5Etfw">January 26, 2026</a></blockquote>
</div></figure>



<p>If adoption grows, EIP-8025 could make full-verifying nodes viable on laptops again and scale Ethereum&rsquo;s base layer without sacrificing decentralization or security.</p>



<p>For validators, developers, and users alike, this may be the moment Ethereum&rsquo;s block validation truly enters a new era.</p>



<p>Tomorrow&rsquo;s L1-zkEVM workshop promises a first glimpse at what could become Ethereum&rsquo;s most transformative architectural leap since The Merge.</p>

<h2 class="bic-gutenberg-heading wp-heading wp-block-heading" id="h-october-10-2025-the-largest-long-liquidation-cascade-came-with-signs">October 10, 2025 &mdash; The Largest Long Liquidation Cascade Came With Signs</h2>



<p>On October 10, 2025, more than $19 billion in leveraged positions were taken out, making it the largest liquidation event in crypto history. Although US&ndash;China tariff headlines are often cited as the trigger, market data show that structural weakness was around for weeks. The majority of these liquidations were long-biased, almost $17 billion.</p>

<hr class="wp-block-separator has-alpha-channel-opacity" />



<h3 class="wp-block-heading" id="h-price-extension-and-leverage-expansion-sep-27-oct-5">Price Extension and Leverage Expansion (Sep 27 &rarr; Oct 5)</h3>



<p>Between September 27 and October 5, <a href="https://beincrypto.com/bitcoin-price-bounce-trap-risk-analysis/" rel="noreferrer noopener" target="_blank">Bitcoin rallied</a> from around $109,000 to above $122,000, eventually testing the $126,000 area. This rapid move strengthened bullish sentiment and encouraged aggressive long positioning.</p>



<p>During the same period, open interest rose from roughly $38 billion to more than $47 billion. Leverage was expanding fast, indicating growing dependence on derivatives.</p>



<p><em><strong>Want more token insights like this?&nbsp;Sign up for Editor Harsh Notariya&rsquo;s Daily Crypto Newsletter&nbsp;<a href="https://go.beincrypto.com/4lUzHZj" rel="noreferrer noopener" target="_blank">here</a>.</strong></em></p>



<figure class="wp-block-image size-full"><img alt="October Crypto Crash Build Up" class="wp-image-800448" src="https://assets.beincrypto.com/img/tUvkkYgsDadM-L2eVQSriV6OKOE=/smart/4fda361983b34535b5e4e2addf9cde8c" /><figcaption class="wp-element-caption">October Crypto Crash Build Up: <a href="https://app.santiment.net/charts/gI0BM8sU__sCl" rel="noreferrer noopener nofollow" target="_blank">Santiment</a></figcaption></figure>



<p>Gracy Chen, the CEO of Bitget, said modern market structure makes leverage far more synchronized than in earlier cycles.</p>



<blockquote class="max-w-xl text-4.5 border-l-2 border-blue-600 pl-11 mb-9 select-all [&amp;_p]:!mb-0 wp-block-quote is-layout-flow wp-block-quote-is-layout-flow">
<p>&ldquo;Positions are built and unwound faster, across more venues&hellip; leverage behaves more synchronously&hellip; When stress hits, the unwind is sharper, more correlated, and less forgiving,&rdquo; she added.</p>
</blockquote>



<p>At the same time, exchange inflows fell from around 68,000 BTC to near 26,000 BTC. Holders were not selling into strength. Instead, supply stayed off exchanges while leveraged exposure increased.</p>



<figure class="wp-block-image size-full"><img alt="October 5 Structure" class="wp-image-800449" src="https://assets.beincrypto.com/img/NJcdsfh_3PD4nVZGld4jvJ7wkj8=/smart/097c51fc1bc5441bb5852ac8ee6c9315" /><figcaption class="wp-element-caption">October 5 Structure: <a href="https://app.santiment.net/charts/gI0BM8sU__sCl" rel="noreferrer noopener nofollow" target="_blank">Santiment</a></figcaption></figure>



<p>This combination reflected a late-stage rally structure.</p>



<p>At this stage of the cycle, rising leverage or open interest, for that matter, not only increases trader risk. It also raises balance-sheet and liquidity pressure on exchanges, which must ensure they can <a href="https://beincrypto.com/2-65-billion-crypto-liquidation-in-feb/" rel="noreferrer noopener" target="_blank">process liquidations</a>, withdrawals, and margin calls smoothly during sudden volatility.</p>



<p>When asked how platforms prepare for such periods, Chen, said risk management starts long before volatility erupts:</p>



<blockquote class="max-w-xl text-4.5 border-l-2 border-blue-600 pl-11 mb-9 select-all [&amp;_p]:!mb-0 wp-block-quote is-layout-flow wp-block-quote-is-layout-flow">
<p>&ldquo;Holding a strong BTC reserve is a risk management decision before it&rsquo;s a market view&hellip; prioritize balance-sheet resilience&hellip; avoid being forced into reactive moves when volatility spikes&hellip;,&rdquo; she said</p>
</blockquote>



<hr class="wp-block-separator has-alpha-channel-opacity" />



<h3 class="wp-block-heading" id="h-profit-taking-beneath-the-surface-late-sep-early-oct">Profit-Taking Beneath the Surface (Late Sep &rarr; Early Oct)</h3>



<p>On-chain profit data showed that distribution had already begun.</p>



<p>From late September into early October, Spent Output Profit Ratio (SOPR), which tracks whether coins are sold at profit or loss, went up from around 1.00 to roughly 1.04, with repeated spikes. This indicated that more coins were being sold at a profit.</p>



<p>Importantly, this happened while exchange inflows remained low. Early buyers (possibly already exchange-held supply) were quietly locking in gains without triggering visible selling pressure. And BTC was already at an all-time high during that time. </p>



<figure class="wp-block-image size-full"><img alt="Post-Peak SOPR" class="wp-image-800450" src="https://assets.beincrypto.com/img/y4hdPMsZtgrB7TASFEwCZtI6rd8=/smart/be4b664e6a8e4245ba1494fbce019650" /><figcaption class="wp-element-caption">Post-Peak SOPR: <a href="https://studio.glassnode.com/charts/indicators.NuplLess155?a=BTC&amp;c=native&amp;mScl=lin&amp;resolution=24h&amp;s=1739114377&amp;u=1770650377&amp;zoom=365" rel="noreferrer noopener nofollow" target="_blank">Glassnode</a></figcaption></figure>



<p>This pattern suggests a gradual transfer from early participants to late entrants, often seen near local tops.</p>



<hr class="wp-block-separator has-alpha-channel-opacity" />



<h3 class="wp-block-heading" id="h-short-term-holders-flip-from-capitulation-to-optimism-september-27-oct-6">Short-Term Holders Flip From Capitulation to Optimism (September 27 &rarr; Oct 6)</h3>



<p>Short-term holder NUPL (Net Unrealized Profit/Loss), measuring paper profits or losses. provided one of the clearest warning signals. On September 27, STH-NUPL stood near -0.17, reflecting recent capitulation. By October 6, it had surged to around +0.09.</p>



<p>In less than ten days, recent buyers moved from heavy losses to clear profits.</p>



<figure class="wp-block-image size-full"><img alt="NUPL Change During Uptrend Can Help Track Long Liquidations" class="wp-image-800451" src="https://assets.beincrypto.com/img/u6_rULQLQdDDPMv8XGCMb8pLjH0=/smart/563b11fe50fc45669b2b20f60ae6c1e4" /><figcaption class="wp-element-capt|https://beincrypto.com/liquidation-cascade-onchain-technical-analysis/|etf,regulation,macro,institutional,layer2,whale,selloff,pump|BTC,ETH,SOL,NEAR,OP,TRX|neutral|1.0|1770720436049
beincrypto_1770737992000_1796041|1770737992000|2026|2|7|2026-02-10|beincrypto|When Is the Right Time to Buy the Crypto Dip? Santiment Highlights 5 Key Signals|<p><strong>The crypto market capitalization has fallen more than 20% year-to-date. In February, investors are divided over whether prices are approaching a local bottom or whether the broader bear market still has room to run. </strong></p>



<p>Amid persistent volatility and growing uncertainty, a key question remains: when is the right time to buy the dip? Analytics platform Santiment has outlined 5 signals to help traders.&nbsp;</p>



<h2 class="bic-gutenberg-heading wp-heading wp-block-heading" id="h-are-traders-missing-buy-signals-during-market-fear-santiment-shares-5-signals">Are Traders Missing Buy Signals During Market Fear? Santiment Shares 5 Signals</h2>



<p>According to Santiment, the first indicator comes from extreme <a href="https://beincrypto.com/crypto-sentiment-extreme-fear-january-2026/" rel="noreferrer noopener" target="_blank">negative social sentiment</a>. By measuring the balance of pessimistic and optimistic language tied directly to specific assets, traders can better filter out noise and identify moments when fear dominates discourse.</p>



<p>Sharp spikes in fear, uncertainty, and doubt (FUD) <a href="https://beincrypto.com/learn/what-is-fud/" rel="noreferrer noopener" target="_blank">and pessimistic commentary</a> across social media in past instances have been followed by market rebounds.</p>



<blockquote class="max-w-xl text-4.5 border-l-2 border-blue-600 pl-11 mb-9 select-all [&amp;_p]:!mb-0 wp-block-quote is-layout-flow wp-block-quote-is-layout-flow">
<p>&ldquo;Bottoming out at $60,001 back on Thursday, cryptocurrency&rsquo;s top market cap asset rebounded a staggering +19% in just under 24 hours following the FUD,&rdquo; the post read. &ldquo;When negativity gets high, it&rsquo;s usually because prices are getting low in a hurry. And once you see the predictions of doom for cryptocurrency, it&rsquo;s generally the best time to officially buy the dip.&rdquo;</p>
</blockquote>



<figure class="wp-block-image size-full"><img alt="Negative Commentary as a Dip Buying Signal" class="wp-image-800769" src="https://assets.beincrypto.com/img/R-lpPwH9fVcJUXhnsv5ltG-8ey0=/smart/f7fd22ddbc2d40e7a02091ba41da4357" /><figcaption class="wp-element-caption">Negative Commentary as a Dip Buying Signal. Source: <a href="https://app.santiment.net/insights/read/deep-dive-finding-buy-signals-while-feeling-rock-bottom-10543" rel="noreferrer noopener nofollow" target="_blank">Santiment</a></figcaption></figure>



<p>Another signal comes from tracking <a href="https://beincrypto.com/crypto-recovery-buy-the-dip/" rel="noreferrer noopener" target="_blank">mentions of phrases</a> such as &ldquo;buy&rdquo;, &ldquo;buying&rdquo;, or &ldquo;bought&rdquo; in association with the word &ldquo;dip.&rdquo; While these mentions increase during sell-offs, Santiment cautions that this metric alone is unreliable. This is because markets can rebound before retail traders fully capitulate.</p>



<p>A more telling sign, according to the platform, is the shift in language from &ldquo;dip&rdquo; to more extreme <a href="https://beincrypto.com/arthur-hayes-explains-what-crashed-bitcoin/" rel="noreferrer noopener" target="_blank">terms like &ldquo;crash.&rdquo; </a>When catastrophic language begins to dominate discussions, it suggests fear-driven capitulation.&nbsp;</p>



<p>Santiment also highlighted the value of monitoring trending bearish keywords. This includes &ldquo;selling,&rdquo; &ldquo;down,&rdquo; or narratives suggesting assets are &ldquo;going to $0,&rdquo; which often emerge when retail confidence breaks.</p>



<p>The final signal comes from on-chain data, specifically the 30-day Market Value to Realized Value (MVRV) ratio. This metric measures whether recently active wallets are, on average, in profit or at a loss. </p>



<p>When MVRV enters the &ldquo;strongly undervalued&rdquo; zone, it indicates that the most recent buyers are underwater. This condition could precede market rebounds.</p>



<blockquote class="max-w-xl text-4.5 border-l-2 border-blue-600 pl-11 mb-9 select-all [&amp;_p]:!mb-0 wp-block-quote is-layout-flow wp-block-quote-is-layout-flow">
<p>&ldquo;As the &lsquo;zone&rsquo; graphics indicate, you typically want to avoid being heavily invested in an asset when it is above the &lsquo;Strongly Overvalued Zone.&rsquo; But on the flip side, there is great upside to buying while it is below the &ldquo;Strongly Undervalued Zone.&rdquo; Santiment added.</p>
</blockquote>



<p>The analysis stressed that defining what constitutes a &ldquo;dip&rdquo; largely depends on market context and the timeframe a trader is operating on. A short-term move of around 1.7% may present an opportunity for hourly swing traders.</p>



<p>Nonetheless, the platform noted that most market participants tend to react on a weekly basis. This better reflects the realistic trading bandwidth of the average trader.</p>



<p>Rather than <a href="https://beincrypto.com/learn/mastering-crypto-trading-emotions/" rel="noreferrer noopener" target="_blank">relying on intuition or &ldquo;anecdotal things,&rdquo;</a> the firm argues that objective data offers clearer insight into when fear-driven sell-offs may be nearing exhaustion.</p>



<p>It is worth noting that buying decisions ultimately depend on individual investor preferences and time horizons. While Santiment&rsquo;s signals can help identify periods of heightened fear and potential opportunity, they do not guarantee that a market rebound will follow.&nbsp;</p>



<p>At present, many <a href="https://beincrypto.com/crypto-market-sentiment-bearish-2026-analysis/" rel="noreferrer noopener" target="_blank">analysts suggest that</a> the broader bear market may <a href="https://beincrypto.com/bitcoin-four-year-halving-cycle-analysis/" rel="noreferrer noopener" target="_blank">still have room to run</a>. This means that prices could remain under pressure for longer.&nbsp;</p>



<p>As a result, decisions to buy or hold should be guided by each investor&rsquo;s risk tolerance, strategy, and opportunity cost considerations.</p>

<h2 class="bic-gutenberg-heading wp-heading wp-block-heading" id="h-bitcoin-profitable-supply-hits-2022-level">Bitcoin Profitable Supply Hits 2022 Level</h2>



<p>Bitcoin&rsquo;s recent decline triggered a signal last seen during the 2022 bear market. The percentage of supply in profit fell to around 50%, meaning half of all circulating <a href="https://beincrypto.com/bitcoin-four-year-halving-cycle-analysis/" rel="noreferrer noopener" target="_blank">BTC is now underwater</a>. This threshold has historically coincided with market bottoms rather than prolonged sell-offs.</p>



<p>When profitable supply compresses to these levels, selling incentives weaken. Holders become less willing to realize losses, reducing sell-side pressure. In previous cycles, this dynamic encouraged investors to hold through volatility, allowing the price to stabilize before recovery resumed.</p>

<p>Currently, the opposite setup is unfolding. The shorter moving average is diverging below the longer one, signaling cooling conditions rather than excess speculation. In past cycles, such divergence often preceded sustained rebounds as Bitcoin reset from overheated levels.</p>

<p>This cycle differs from prior ones. Since March 2023, Bitcoin has maintained a macro uptrend without excessive overheating. Gradual price appreciation limited speculative excess, making this the first clear bottom signal in nearly three years rather than a sharp capitulation-driven low.</p>

Trading infrastructure has gone digital, execution is instantaneous, and information moves globally in real time. <h2 class="bic-gutenberg-heading wp-heading wp-block-heading" id="h-spot-trading-vs-futures-contracts">Spot trading vs futures contracts</h2>



<p>Spot and futures markets work differently, and that difference explains why TradFi futures matter. Put simply, spot trading means you buy the asset itself at the current price, whereas a futures contract tracks price under contract terms rather than giving direct ownership.</p>



<p>In traditional spot trading, buying a share or commodity involves a complex chain of custody, legal ownership transfer, and T+2 settlement cycles. This infrastructure requires banks and clearinghouses to be open, which is why trading halts on weekends and holidays.</p>



<p>A futures contract is a derivative, an agreement based on the price of an asset, not the exchange of the asset itself. Because of this, there is no physical action or need for a transfer in the event of a closed exchange market.</p>



<p>When the market closes, only the conventional infrastructure ceases to function; assets retain their worth.<strong> Phemex fills this gap by delivering a marketplace where price discovery and risk management continue uninterrupted.</strong></p>



<h2 class="bic-gutenberg-heading wp-heading wp-block-heading" id="h-macro-news-don-t-wait-for-monday">Macro News Don&rsquo;t Wait for Monday</h2>



<p>Traditional finance (TradFi) and cryptocurrency markets are increasingly moving in the same direction. As crypto trading has matured, digital asset prices have become more closely linked to macroeconomic indicators that have long driven equities and commodities.</p>



<p>Interest rate decisions by the U.S. Federal Reserve, inflation data, labor market reports, and geopolitical developments now influence both stock indices and major cryptocurrencies. This growing correlation has reshaped how traders think about risk, timing, and market access across asset classes.</p>



<p>The introduction of TradFi futures on crypto-native trading platforms allows traders to respond to macroeconomic developments in real time. Instead of waiting for traditional market hours, traders can hedge positions or manage volatility as events unfold&mdash;an approach that is increasingly central to modern risk management.</p>



<p>Whether it is hedging a position or capitalizing on volatility, the ability to execute trades based on real-time macro news is no longer a luxury,; it is a necessity for modern risk management.</p>



<h2 class="bic-gutenberg-heading wp-heading wp-block-heading" id="h-why-tradfi-futures-matter-for-24-7-market-access">Why TradFi Futures Matter for 24/7 Market Access</h2>



<p>The 24/7 openness of markets, remaining functional even during holidays and non-working days, is not merely a new generation innovation; it represents the natural evolutionary progression of trading. In the traditional financial world, when the market is closed, uncertainty and suspense tend to take hold.&nbsp;</p>



<p>If a major event occurs over the weekend, traditional investors face significant gap risk, where the price jumps or drops substantially between Friday&rsquo;s close and Monday&rsquo;s open.</p>



<p>Through TradFi futures trading found on Phemex, traders can manage their positions at any time, day or night. This eliminates the waiting game that often leaves investors vulnerable to global news cycles that do not stop for bank holidays.</p>



<h2 class="bic-gutenberg-heading wp-heading wp-block-heading" id="h-unified-trading-across-crypto-and-tradfi-futures-on-a-single-platform-nbsp">Unified Trading Across Crypto and TradFi Futures on a Single Platform&nbsp;</h2>



<p><strong>Phemex</strong> focuses on reducing the liquidity and access friction typical of traditional markets.</p>



<p>The platform offers <a href="https://phemex.com/tradfi?group=8127&amp;referralCode=CUFKP8" rel="noreferrer noopener nofollow" target="_blank"><strong>USDT-settled derivatives</strong> </a>linked to traditional assets such as gold, silver, and selected stocks, alongside crypto derivatives. This structure allows traders to access multiple asset classes from a single account, without opening separate brokerage relationships or navigating lengthy funding and settlement processes.</p>



<p>(USDT-settled derivatives mean that profits and losses are settled in USDT rather than through delivery of the underlying asset.)</p>



<p>Phemex operates a <strong>unified margin system</strong>, enabling the same USDT balance to be used across gold, silver, and crypto futures. Because these contracts track price rather than involve physical settlement, custody and operational complexity are reduced.</p>



<p>As with cryptocurrency perpetual contracts, TradFi futures can be traded with leverage, allowing traders to increase exposure and improve capital efficiency without committing the full notional amount typically required by traditional brokers. Historically, access to equities or commodities&mdash;whether via direct ownership, ETFs, or futures&mdash;often required substantial upfront capital and fragmented infrastructure.</p>



<p>As demand grows for continuous market access and more flexible risk management, crypto-native platforms are increasingly addressing these structural limitations. Phemex positions itself within this shift by offering infrastructure designed for continuous, multi-asset trading.</p>



<h2 class="bic-gutenberg-heading wp-heading wp-block-heading" id="h-the-modern-market-is-open-24-7">The Modern Market Is Open 24/7</h2>



<p>Market evolution is no longer a question of <em>if</em>, but <em>how</em>. As crypto and traditional assets increasingly respond to the same macro forces, their separation at the infrastructure level has started to break down.</p>



<p>The objective isn&rsquo;t to replicate stock exchanges on crypto platforms. It&rsquo;s to build faster, more flexible systems that allow traders to access traditional asset exposure with the efficiency they expect from modern markets.</p>



<p><strong>Phemex</strong> is approaching this by replacing ownership friction with futures-based access. By using price-tracking contracts rather than physical settlement, traditional assets can be traded alongside crypto within a unified, USDT-settled environment.</p>



<p>Moving into the second quarter of 2026, trading across asset classes from a single margin currency is no longer a differentiator; it&rsquo;s becoming the baseline for how modern markets operate.</p>



<p><em>As part of the launch of its TradFi futures offering, </em><strong><em>Phemex</em></strong><em> has </em><a href="https://phemex.com/en/events/token-fiesta/836?group=8127&amp;referralCode=CUFKP8" rel="noreferrer noopener nofollow" target="_blank"><em>introduced</em></a><em> a limited-time campaign aimed at familiarizing traders with the new product. <figure class="wp-block-image size-full"><img alt="Ethereum (ETH) Price Performance" class="wp-image-800728" src="https://assets.beincrypto.com/img/PwaQ7TwV0sgEfx6DN7lmad6ppDE=/smart/6d4bde3b3c7941b288e06cbeca9541a5" /><figcaption class="wp-element-caption">Ethereum (ETH) Price Performance. Source:<a href="https://beincrypto.com/price/ethereum/" rel="noreferrer noopener" target="_blank"> BeInCrypto Markets</a></figcaption></figure>



<p>Lee suggested that the company views the price<a href="https://beincrypto.com/bitmine-ethereum-losses-defended-lee/" rel="noreferrer noopener" target="_blank"> pullback as a strategic</a> buying opportunity, citing improving network fundamentals.</p>



<p>He also noted network strength despite falling prices. Ethereum daily transactions hit 2.5 million and active addresses reached 1 million in 2026, as stated in BitMine&rsquo;s official announcement. These figures imply rising adoption regardless of market swings.</p>



<blockquote class="max-w-xl text-4.5 border-l-2 border-blue-600 pl-11 mb-9 select-all [&amp;_p]:!mb-0 wp-block-quote is-layout-flow wp-block-quote-is-layout-flow">
<p>&ldquo;In our view, the price of ETH is not reflective of the high utility of ETH and its role as the future of finance,&rdquo; he <a href="https://www.prnewswire.com/news-releases/bitmine-immersion-technologies-bmnr-announces-eth-holdings-reach-4-326-million-tokens-and-total-crypto-and-total-cash-holdings-of-10-0-billion-302682272.html" rel="noreferrer noopener nofollow" target="_blank">said</a>.</p>
</blockquote>



<p>Furthermore, Lee pointed to Ethereum&rsquo;s historical price behavior to support his optimism. Since 2018, ETH has experienced 8 separate declines of 50% or more from recent highs.</p>



<p>He highlighted a similar pattern in 2025, when Ethereum fell by 64% between January and March before rallying sharply later in the year. At the time, it surged from approximately $1,600 to nearly $5,000.</p>



<p>According to Lee, Ethereum has historically staged V-shaped recoveries following major downturns. He stated that such rebounds occurred after each of the previous 8 drawdowns. Based on this trend, he expects a comparable recovery <a href="https://beincrypto.com/tom-lee-bitcoin-bottom-us-crypto-news/" rel="noreferrer noopener" target="_blank">to unfold in 2026</a>.</p>



<blockquote class="max-w-xl text-4.5 border-l-2 border-blue-600 pl-11 mb-9 select-all [&amp;_p]:!mb-0 wp-block-quote is-layout-flow wp-block-quote-is-layout-flow">
<p>&ldquo;The best investment opportunities in crypto have presented themselves after declines. Think back to 2025, the single best entry points in crypto occurred after markets fell sharply due to tariff concerns,&rdquo; Lee stated.</p>
</blockquote>
